     <p>The following is a list of <b>potential datasources</b>. Some of these are already in use, or have been imported fully. Others are under investigation, and some have been rejected (details of rejections are on here too). There are basically two criteria: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <b>Licenses</b> - We are only interested in 'free' data. In fact we must be able to release their data with our <a href="/wiki/OpenStreetMap_License" title="OpenStreetMap License">OpenStreetMap License</a>. <b>This means it's OK to use Public Domain data</b>; for other sources, please check license compatibility.</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> <b>Accuracy/Quality</b> - All GIS data is limited in terms of <a href="/wiki/Accuracy" title="Accuracy">accuracy</a> and coverage of features. Some datasources are very basic. Because of our wiki style map building approach, this isn't necessarily a problem. We could import it anyway, and improve it later. However there are limits to this reasoning, it does for example require active OSM community members for the area affected. Also in areas where we already have superior coverage through other means, we will not be interested in importing lower quality data. For example a low accuracy map of the main roads of London, is actually useless to us, whereas similar coverage of an unmapped city would be useful.</li>
     </ul> 
     <p>With these criteria in mind, look at the following, see if there are license issues and if they are useful to us or we can collaborate, and mail the <a href="/wiki/Mailing_lists" title="Mailing lists">Mailing lists</a> with results. Freegis.org is compiling a similar list <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://freegis.org/database/?cat=1">[2]</a>, but it doesn't contain everything. </p>
     <p>Listing datasources here is only the first stage in a careful investigation/planning process for <a href="/wiki/Imports" class="mw-redirect" title="Imports">imports</a>. If you're interested in performing imports please be aware: </p> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox" style="margin:2px 10%;background:#FDD;border:1px solid #AAA;border-left:10px #B22222 solid;">
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image" style="border:none;padding:2px 0;padding-left:0.9em;text-align:center">
         <div style="width:52px;">
          <img alt="Warning" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/40px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png" title="Warning" width="40" height="35" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/60px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/80px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png 2x">
         </div></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style="width:100%;border:none;padding:0.25em 0.9em;text-align:center;">Imports and automated edits should only be carried out by those with experience and understanding of the way the OpenStreetMap community creates maps, and only with careful <b>planning</b> and <b>consultation</b> with the local community.<br> See <a href="/wiki/Import/Guidelines" title="Import/Guidelines">Import/Guidelines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automated_Edits_code_of_conduct" title="Automated Edits code of conduct">Automated Edits code of conduct</a> for more information. Imports/automated edits which do not follow these guidelines might be reverted!</td> 
       </tr>
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Datasources which we have imported should also go on the <a href="/wiki/Import/Catalogue" title="Import/Catalogue">Import/Catalogue</a>. We also have a list of <a href="/wiki/Related_Projects" title="Related Projects">Related Projects</a> </p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Out-of-copyright_mapping">Out-of-copyright mapping</span></h3> 
     <p>See separate page on <a href="/wiki/Out-of-copyright_maps" title="Out-of-copyright maps">out-of-copyright maps</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dispatch_centres">Dispatch centres</span></h3> 
     <p>Many transportation companies (Taxi, delivery, courier services) are using GPS units in their vehicles either to track them in real time in their dispatching centre or just for logging. It should be in their interest to provide their GPS tracks in order to improve the maps in their areas of operation. Taxis should effectively cover a city fast, while lorries and such are probably better for longer distances. Already using <a href="/wiki/Ecourier" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecourier">Ecourier</a> tracks. </p>
     <p><br> </p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Coverage">Global Coverage</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Port_Index_.28position_and_data_of_harbours_worldwide.29">World Port Index (position and data of harbours worldwide)</span></h3> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://msi.nga.mil/NGAPortal/MSI.portal?_nfpb=true&amp;_st=&amp;_pageLabel=msi_portal_page_62&amp;pubCode=0015">National Geospatial-Intelligence Agency WPI</a> - © COPYRIGHT 2015 BY THE UNITED STATES GOVERNMENT NO COPYRIGHT CLAIMED UNDER TITLE 17 U.S.C.</li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Perry-Casta.C3.B1eda_Library_Map_Collection_.28contains_Army_Map_Service_Topographic_Map_Series.29">Perry-Castañeda Library Map Collection (contains Army Map Service Topographic Map Series)</span></h3> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/">http://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_CIA_World_DataBank">The CIA World DataBank</span></h3> 
     <p>The CIA World DataBank II is a collection of world map data, consisting of vector descriptions of land outlines, rivers, and political boundaries. It was created by the U.S. government in 1986. Hence it should be under public domain, since the files haven't changed since. There's roughly 1.8 million shape points in Europe and N.A. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.evl.uic.edu/pape/data/WDB/">http://www.evl.uic.edu/pape/data/WDB/</a> </li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.evl.uic.edu/pape/data/WDB/WDB-text.tar.gz">http://www.evl.uic.edu/pape/data/WDB/WDB-text.tar.gz</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <p>GPX files can be created from the CIA World DataBank with the Perl script at </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20110719172943/http://www.ces.clemson.edu/~sadam/gpx">archive.org version of http://www.ces.clemson.edu/~sadam/gpx</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <p>There is now an 0.5-compatible import script for OSM at <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://trac.openstreetmap.org/browser/applications/utils/import/wdb2osm">[3]</a>. Please document your upload progress on <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_Import_WDB" title="WikiProject Import WDB">WikiProject_Import_WDB</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GEOnet_Names_Server">GEOnet Names Server</span></h3> 
     <p><i>Main page <a href="/wiki/GEOnet_Names_Server" title="GEOnet Names Server">GEOnet Names Server</a></i> </p>
     <p>This database contains 5.5 million geo features (mainly place names). It's updated monthly by the agency. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://earth-info.nga.mil/gns/html">http://earth-info.nga.mil/gns/html</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://earth-info.nga.mil/gns/html/cntyfile/gm.zip">http://earth-info.nga.mil/gns/html/cntyfile/gm.zip</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="ftp://ftp.nima.mil/pub/gns_data/">ftp://ftp.nima.mil/pub/gns_data/</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://earth-info.nga.mil/gns/html/whatsnew.htm#C3">'about' page</a> states </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <i> "There are no licensing requirements or restrictions in place for the use of the GNS data. However, we recommend using the following citation to identify the GNS as a source ...</i>
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <p>The data is messy and with spelling mistakes and strange historical name entries. Accuracy is also poor. We have imported GNS data in some countries, usually where mapping is not progressing massively anyway. This hasn't been carried out systematically at a global level. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geonames.org_.28Rejected.29">Geonames.org (Rejected)</span></h3> 
     <p><i>Main page: <a href="/wiki/Geonames" title="Geonames">Geonames</a></i> </p>
     <p>This is a "wiki" style name server at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.geonames.org/">geonames.org</a> which claims to release data with an open license, however it uses various unfree datasources, and pinpoints locations on an unfree google map. It therefore does not meet the strict requirements of OSM </p>
     <p>We do use the dataset for <a href="/wiki/Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Search">Search</a> however </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Map_Library">The Map Library</span></h3> 
     <p>The Map Library is a source of public domain basic map data concerning administrative boundaries in developing countries. The format of available data is Map Maker DRA, ESRI Shape file or MapInfo MIF. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maplibrary.org/stacks/Africa/index.php">Africa</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maplibrary.org/stacks/Central%20America/index.php">Central America</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <p>In addition to the Map Library data they also are hosting a copy of version 0.9 of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maplibrary.org/stacks/gadm/index.php">Global Administrative Areas</a> database of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biogeomancer.org/">BioGeoMancer</a> project, but: </p>
     <p><b>Note:</b> The administrative areas dataset is licensed under a <i>noncommercial creative commons license</i>, so it <b>cannot be used</b> in OpenStreetMap. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://maplibrary.org/stacks/gadm/index.php">[4]</a> </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> The homepage is <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.maplibrary.org/">http://www.maplibrary.org/</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OpenGeoDB">OpenGeoDB</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/OpenGeoDB" title="OpenGeoDB">OpenGeoDB</a> was started as a German project for places within Germany, extended to Austria, Switzerland, Liechtenstein and Belgium by now. Initial data was derived from GEOnet Names Server, but has been extended by postal area codes, population, governmental structure etc. </p>
     <p>The data is public domain and can be used without any limitations. </p>
     <p>The homepage is <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://opengeodb.de">http://opengeodb.de</a> </p>
     <p>Dumps are released on sourceforge: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://sourceforge.net/projects/opengeodb/">http://sourceforge.net/projects/opengeodb/</a> </p>
     <p>Data can be edited and downloaded any time via <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://fa-technik.adfc.de/code/opengeodb.pl">http://fa-technik.adfc.de/code/opengeodb.pl</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Berkeley_BioGeo_gData_set">The Berkeley BioGeo gData set</span></h3> 
     <p>See <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_BioGeo_data" title="Berkeley BioGeo data">Berkeley_BioGeo_data</a> for more details of this many-country database. It concerns ESRI compatible <i>free</i> data, in which free needs to be examined. It is presumed that ESRI compatible files can be converted into OSM formats, even when ESRI itself is a company. Is a dataformat leading to a problem with licenses? <a href="/wiki/User:Orwall" title="User:Orwall">Orwall</a> 24 Jan 2008 </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <b>This data set uses a blanket CC-BY-NC-SA. The NC part makes it incompatible with OSM. Individual parts of the database have additional restrictions, and there may be an overall database right being infringed. We may need to look at purging what has already been imported.</b> 
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Chriscf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Chriscf (page does not exist)">Chriscf</a> 09:10, 21 October 2008 (UTC)
      </dd> 
      <dd>
       I'll investigate the part containing global administrative areas (but called 
       <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://biogeo.berkeley.edu/gadm/">GADM</a>). It seems to be very useful, because administrative boundaries are missing for large parts of the world. One table in the geodatabase (MS Access) contains information on copyright for every country. I'll try to contact one of the persons at Berkeley, and ask if they agree to lift the NC restriction for OSM. --
       <a href="/wiki/User:Fsteggink" title="User:Fsteggink">Fsteggink</a> 16:32, 14 February 2009 (UTC)
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shoreline_databases">Shoreline databases</span></h3> 
     <p>There are several freely available datasets for coastlines. For paths running along cliff tops you wouldn't want to trust your life to any of this data - but for the purposes of giving you a plausible landmass to draw maps on they're all useful. See <a href="/wiki/Proposed_features/Coastline" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposed features/Coastline">Proposed features/Coastline</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prototype_Global_Shoreline">Prototype Global Shoreline</span></h4> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <i>See the main page on <a href="/wiki/Prototype_Global_Shoreline" title="Prototype Global Shoreline">PGS</a></i>
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <p>Our script for importing into the OSM database is "<a href="/wiki/Almien_coastlines_(PGS)" title="Almien coastlines (PGS)">Almien coastlines (PGS)</a>" </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="GSHHS_-_Global_Self-consistent_Hierarchical_High-resolution_Shoreline">GSHHS - Global Self-consistent Hierarchical High-resolution Shoreline</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ngdc.noaa.gov/mgg/shorelines/gshhs.html">http://www.ngdc.noaa.gov/mgg/shorelines/gshhs.html</a> </p>
     <p>Import script is at <a href="/wiki/Almien_coastlines_(GSHHS)" title="Almien coastlines (GSHHS)">Almien coastlines (GSHHS)</a>, but is not being used in favour of PGS. </p>
     <p>GSHHS is a database of lakes and shorelines of the world, resolution of 200m produced in 1996. Delivered with source, written in C, and the PD database. They are also available as shapefiles. Tends to give more accurate coastlines than VMAP0 outside of the US (for some reason VMAP0 seems more accurate for the US). There are issues with inland water (such as the great lakes) though. </p>
     <p>(The above info appears slightly incorrect: according to the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="ftp://ftp.soest.hawaii.edu/pwessel/gshhs/README.gshhs">README</a> the last update was in 2004. It was generated from the CIA WDBII and the WVS). </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="VMAP0">VMAP0</span></h4> 
     <p>US department of defence vector map (contains far more than just coastlines, but can be rather "coarse". Also known as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maproom.psu.edu/dcw/">Digital Chart of the World</a>. See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vector_Map">Wikipedia</a>. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Vector_Shoreline">World Vector Shoreline</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ngdc.noaa.gov/mgg/coast/wvs.html">http://www.ngdc.noaa.gov/mgg/coast/wvs.html</a> </p>
     <p>Claims, 1:250,000 scale use, seems pretty accurate at least for the GB and Ireland </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EVS_Islands_.28Data_Dependent.29">EVS Islands (Data Dependent)</span></h4> 
     <p>Based upon different landsat images, some comparisons are made against <a href="/wiki/Prototype_Global_Shoreline" title="Prototype Global Shoreline">PGS</a>, and there are also maps traced from Google Earth imagery. He makes very beautiful maps of all the islands of the world. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://evs-islands.blogspot.com">http://evs-islands.blogspot.com</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="SWBD_-_Shuttle_radar_topography_mission_Water_Body_Data.">SWBD - Shuttle radar topography mission Water Body Data.</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="ftp://e0srp01u.ecs.nasa.gov/srtm/version2">ftp://e0srp01u.ecs.nasa.gov/srtm/version2</a> </p>
     <p>Derived from the SRTM digital elevation model. Newer than the rest, potentially more accurate. </p>
     <p>From the README: SRTM data are distributed in two levels: SRTM1 (for the U.S. and its territories and possessions) with data sampled at one arc-second intervals in latitude and longitude, and SRTM3 (for the world) sampled at three arc-seconds. Three arc-second data are generated by three by three averaging of the one arc-second samples. </p>
     <p>For reference: one arc-second at the equator is 30metres. For the US this means around 18m accuracy, but for elsewhere it's pretty bad. At the latitude of Brussels it would be about 60metres accuracy. For any latitude l, 1 arc-second of longitude is about 30 metres multiplied by cos(l). </p>
     <p>The SWBD data is derived from this and claims one-arc second accuracy worldwide, though only lakes greater than 200m are included. </p>
     <p>Converting SRTM into OSM format can be done with <a href="/wiki/Srtm2Osm" title="Srtm2Osm">Srtm2Osm</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Earth_Observing_Laboratory_NCAR.">Earth Observing Laboratory NCAR.</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eol.ucar.edu/">EOL</a> provides state-of-the-art atmospheric observing systems and support services to the university-based research community for climate and weather research. Most of it is free(?) </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> Unless I misunderstand the OSM license, this <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ucar.edu/legal/terms_of_use.shtml">quote</a> from <b>Prohibited Uses</b> on the NCAR terms page would seem to indicate data cannot be used without a special wavier being granted by them for the possibility of their data being used in a work that is sold. Other conditions may apply too. Data from here should wait until the new OSM licensing is decided so that we don't have to risk them not agreeing to the new requirements after data under the old agreement has been imported.</li>
     </ul> 
     <blockquote>
       "
      <i>Use that is inconsistent with UCAR's non-profit status and mission. UCAR is a non-profit, tax-exempt organization and, as such, is subject to specific federal, state, and local laws regarding sources of income, political activities, use of property, and similar matters. As a result, commercial use of this Site or the Materials for non-UCAR purposes is generally prohibited. Requests for exception to this should be directed to ipinfo@ucar.edu.</i>" 
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Rjhawkin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Rjhawkin (page does not exist)">Rjhawkin</a> 09:35, 18 April 2009 (UTC)
     </blockquote> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ICEDS_European_Data_Server">ICEDS European Data Server</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://iceds.ge.ucl.ac.uk/viewer/iceds/index.html">ICEDS server</a> is hosted and run from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ge.ucl.ac.uk/">UCL</a> with the aim of serving high-resolution global and continental data. One of the nicest things about the site is its ease of use - you view an area and then click a button to download the relevant data (SRTM, Geological Maps, Landsat 5 &amp; 7, etc). The site is also an exercise in Open Standards and is fully compliant with the OGC's WMS, WFS standards - meaning that a variety of external data sources (Weather and bathymetry for example) can be overlaid with the click of a button (Why not OSM data?). In common with OSM it is also based on an Open source principle - Map Server on Apache on Linux. </p>
     <p>Two things I particularly like about the site: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>Extensive use of Java-Script embeds a lot of features onto the page. Try out the "Flicker" and "Swipe" tools and the drop down menus for downloading SRTM data.</li> 
      <li>The near realtime (15 minute delay I think) Global Clouds layer.</li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="hostip.info_Geolocation_data">hostip.info Geolocation data</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.hostip.info/">http://www.hostip.info/</a> has a geolocation database. <a href="/wiki/Geolocation" title="Geolocation">Geolocation</a> means mapping from IP address to location. It's a neat trick, although the accuracy is obviously quite variable (try it on the site there) We could try to use this to jump to the user's home town, rather than the default world map, when a visitor enters the openstreetmap.org homepage. Might fun, or it might just be confusing when it gets it wrong. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ip_Global_Positioning_.28Unfree.29">Ip Global Positioning (Unfree)</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ipgp.net">http://www.ipgp.net</a> will show a map with the location of an IP address. In some cases it will show the location of Internet Service Provider, but you can still make an idea. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DAFIF">DAFIF</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DAFIF">Defense Aeronautical Flight Information File</a>. Published by the US Department of Defense, lists pretty much every airport runway worldwide. Apparently, they're going to be removing the dataset from public domain in October 2006. This is used to populate the scenery databases for <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.flightgear.org">Flightgear flight simulator</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://x-plane.org/">X-Plane</a>. Whilst the dataset is still being kept updated in the public domain, I'll work out an import to Openstreetmap of the runways and taxiways. <a href="/wiki/User:Welshie" title="User:Welshie">Welshie</a> 09:51, 25 Jun 2006 (UTC) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ourairports.com">ourairports.com</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ourairports.com/data/">ourairports.com</a> is a replacement for some of the DAFIF data, put into in the public domain. </p>

     <ul>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="APRS_data">APRS data</span></h3> 
     <p>Many Amateur radio operators have GPS receivers connected to packet radio transmitters and transmit their location in a standard format known as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automatic_Position_Reporting_System">APRS</a> (including fixed stations, weather stations, and mobile stations) on standard frequencies from which the data can be picked up and is injected into a internet infrastructure <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aprs-is.net/overview.htm">APRS-IS</a>. The infrastructure includes databases <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aprsworld.net/">APRSWorld</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.openaprs.net/">OpenAPRS</a>, and a substantial supporting body of open source software (which would make it simple to set up a database to selectively mine internet feeds for data coming from mobile stations that are likely to be traveling on roads). APRS data does have some intrinsic limitations - positions are usually transmitted on 5-10 minute intervals, and a widely used non-compressed format limits the precision of latitude and longitude to 0.01 minute (see the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tapr.org/aprs_working_group.html">APRS protocol specification</a> for details). Given the origin of APRS data as Amateur radio transmissions, they are likely to be in the public domain. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> APRS is more a use specific data point. A potential problem is that some APRS stations are not following a land based track. I know of several APRS devices mounted to weather balloons, hot air balloons, regular and RC aircraft, or boats. There is no requirement to indicate to a third party what use your APRS station is being put to when it transmits a packet.<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Rjhawkin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Rjhawkin (page does not exist)">Rjhawkin</a> 09:52, 18 April 2009 (UTC)</li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Placeopedia_.28rejected.29">Placeopedia (rejected)</span></h3> 
     <p>The guys who gave us <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.pledgebank.com/">Pledgebank </a> made <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.placeopedia.com/">placeopedia</a> as well, it's a way to use Google maps to geo reference wikipedia articles. The database is held separately from the wikipedia one, and can be accessed with rss, xml and kml feeds from their site. </p>
     <p>It <i>says</i> it is available under a Creative Commons license, but not which one. </p>
     <p>This has been discussed on the mailing list, and the consensus is that Placeopedia is a derivative work of Google Maps. Although it's very unlikely to be challenged by Google Maps / Teleatlas, it's <b>not suitable for use in OpenStreetMap</b> (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk/2005-October/001212.html">http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk/2005-October/001212.html</a> is one of many relevant posts, and a good summary of the argument). </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SALB">SALB</span></h3> 
     <p>"The Second Administrative Level Boundaries (SALB) dataset is a dataset aiming at improving the availability of information about administrative boundaries down to the second subnational level. The SALB dataset forms part of the UN geographic database and was developed in the context of the United Nations Geographic Information Working Group (UNGIWG)." </p>
     <p><a href="/wiki/SALB" title="SALB">SALB</a> </p>
     <p><br> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="True_Marble_imagery_.28Unearthed_Outdoors.29">True Marble imagery (Unearthed Outdoors)</span></h3> 
     <p>Full color global imagery, built from the best available Landsat scenes which have been chosen to optimize vegetation quality and to reduce the cloud cover. These orthorectified scenes were fed into proprietary, advanced, color adjustment algorithms to produce true color imagery while reducing atmospheric haze. This imagery was optimized to produce the most natural color while maintaining a high local contrast and dynamic range, resulting in a significant improvement over similar products. </p>
     <p>A reduced resolution of the True Marble™, Global True Marble™, is available for free download. This dataset can be used to preview pending purchases, or for any other usage. We only ask that copyright be attributed to Unearthed Outdoors when reproduced. </p>
     <p>Licensed under a<b> Creative Commons Attribution 3.0</b> United States License. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.unearthedoutdoors.net/global_data/true_marble/download">http://www.unearthedoutdoors.net/global_data/true_marble/download</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Database_on_Protected_Areas_.28WDPA.29_.28Rejected.29">World Database on Protected Areas (WDPA) (Rejected)</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.wdpa.org/Default.aspx">http://www.wdpa.org/Default.aspx</a> </p>
     <p>"The World Database on Protected Areas is a foundation dataset for conservation decision making. It contains crucial information from national governments, non-governmental organizations, academic institutions, international biodiversity convention secretariats and many others. It is used for ecological gap analysis, environmental impact analysis and is increasingly used for private sector decision-making...." </p>
     <p><a href="/wiki/WDPA_data_use_email_request" title="WDPA data use email request">WDPA data use email request</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ramsar_Wetland_Sites">Ramsar Wetland Sites</span></h3> 
     <p>The data included in the database derives from the Ramsar Information Sheet, the Ramsar National Report and/or from Administrative Authority correspondence provided by Contracting Parties. This includes information on wetland types, land uses, threats, hydrological values of the sites etc. The Ramsar Sites Database is primarily a tool to look at Ramsar Sites across geographic and thematic boundaries, useful and necessary for maintaining an overview of a global network of well over 1700 internationally important wetlands from 158 countries. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ramsar.wetlands.org/GISMaps/DownloadGISdatasets/tabid/769/language/en-US/Default.aspx">Ramsar Sites Information Service</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ramsar.wetlands.org/Home/tabid/719/ctl/Terms/Default.aspx">Terms of Use @ wetland.org</a></li> 
      <li> See referencing mail correspondence <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk/2009-September/042488.html">[5]</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OpenCellID_cell">OpenCellID cell</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.opencellid.org/">http://www.opencellid.org/</a> <br> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://wiki.opencellid.org">http://wiki.opencellid.org</a> </p>
     <p>OpenCellID is the biggest open source data for CellIDs (GPS positions of cell towers), and provides an API to both<br> - gather data of newly discovered cell towers <br> - locate a cell phone or tracking device using cell tower positions </p>
     <p>Source code is provided under a GPL license, while data is collected under a Creative Commons Share Alike license V3.0 </p>
     <p>Plans exist to support Wifi/Bluetooth positioning. </p>
     <p>see also: <a href="/wiki/OpenCellID" title="OpenCellID">OpenCellID</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="OpenBmap_cell_and_wifi_access_points">OpenBmap cell and wifi access points</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://realtimeblog.free.fr/">http://realtimeblog.free.fr/</a> </p>
     <p>openBmap is a free and open map of wireless communicating objects (e.g. cellular antenna, Wi-Fi, Bluetooth). It provides tools to mutualize data, create and access this map. </p>
     <p>Data is available under Creative Commons Attribution-Share Alike 3.0 Unported license, and is currently provided as a static download, updated regularly. </p>
     <p>The site owners intend to create an api, which could allow regular, scripted updates to the data. Alternatively, it could be suggested that they adopt their site/software, to upload data direct to osm </p>
     <p>see also: <a href="/wiki/OpenBmap" title="OpenBmap">openBmap</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CODATA_Roads_Data_Catalog">CODATA Roads Data Catalog</span></h3> 
     <p>A catalog of roads data sets, globally, compiled by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ciesin.columbia.edu/confluence/display/roads/Global+Roads+Data">gRoads project</a>. There are hundreds of data sets listed here (many probably already investigated), under all sorts of licensing schemes. There are certainly data sets new to the OSM community that are worth investigating. </p>
     <p>The interim PDF is posted at <a href="/w/images/5/55/CODATA_Roads_Data_Catalog_v1.pdf" class="internal" title="CODATA Roads Data Catalog v1.pdf">Media:CODATA_Roads_Data_Catalog_v1.pdf</a> </p>
     <p>There are possible plans to post this database to the web, with query front end. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_Laws_Of_the_Sea">United Nations Laws Of the Sea</span></h3> 
     <p>The UN DOALOS have a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.un.org/Depts/los/LEGISLATIONANDTREATIES/">database</a> over all maritime border claims. There is no apparent license on the data and this is the borders definitions. But the database is a database of different PDF files with coordinates of baselines and territorial borders. The text has to be parsed by hand and other maritime borders needs to be calculated from the baseline (see <a href="/wiki/Maritime_borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime borders">maritime borders</a>). Data is to be tagged with <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<bdi>UNCLOS</bdi></tt> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freebase">Freebase</span></h3> 
     <p>Though the two projects have significant overlap and are both Creative Commons, they are [ <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://wiki.freebase.com/wiki/License_compatibility#Compatible_licenses_for_structured_data">http://wiki.freebase.com/wiki/License_compatibility#Compatible_licenses_for_structured_data</a> incompatible]. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://Freebase.com">Freebase.com</a> is licenced under CC-BY. The biggest hurdle in using OSM data within Freebase has been the OSM share-alike license. All the data in Freebase is available under a CC-BY (attribution only) license, allowing anyone to use the data in any way they want as along as they acknowledge Freebase. The main difference between the licenses is that the Freebase CC-BY license does not impose a share-alike requirement on users of the data. </p>
     <p>That said, the OSM community is currently voting on an updated license which could make collaboration between the two data sets much easier in the future (for more information see: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Open_Database_License">Open_Database_License</a>) </p>
     <p>In spite of the licence conflict, simply linking these resources together wouldn't be a problem. </p>
     <p>we could connect relations to locations </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>/en/buenos_aires</li> 
      <li>/relation/369450</li>
     </ul> 
     <p>and connect osm'samenity nodes (or 'points of interest'). both databases for example, have a mount sinai hospital- </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>osm @ /node/42606735</li> 
      <li>freebase @ /guid/9202a8c04000641f800000000039b682</li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Marine_Lights">List of Marine Lights</span></h3> 
     <p>This is a database of <i>lights, radio, and fog signals</i>. It contains almost all lights on the world and is published by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://msi.nga.mil/NGAPortal/">US Nationional Geospatiol Intelligency Agency</a> which may have a useful copyright permission. </p>
     <p>The information is published as PDF documents and we have already parsed them into an OSM appropriate format. The tags used for imported are planned to be the <a href="/wiki/OpenSeaMap" title="OpenSeaMap">OpenSeaMap</a> proposed seamark:*=* ones. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EC-JRC_built-up_areas_.2F_density_of_building_from_Bing">EC-JRC built-up areas / density of building from Bing</span></h3> 
     <p>See <a href="/wiki/EC-JRC_built-up_areas_from_Bing" title="EC-JRC built-up areas from Bing">EC-JRC built-up areas from_Bing</a> </p>
     <p>This is partially a follow-up to this thread: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/imports/2011-June/000987.html">http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/imports/2011-June/000987.html</a> </p>
     <p>We (the Joint Research Centre of the European Commission) have developed a set of scripted tools to extract built-up areas, built-up density, and location of human settlements from (very) high resolution satellite imagery. The result is quite reliable and our methodology has been warmly received by the remote sensing community. Part of the methodology is described in this paper: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/search/srchabstract.jsp?tp=&amp;arnumber=5764726">http://ieeexplore.ieee.org/search/srchabstract.jsp?tp=&amp;arnumber=5764726</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Gateway_to_Astronaut_Photography_of_Earth">The Gateway to Astronaut Photography of Earth</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://eol.jsc.nasa.gov/">http://eol.jsc.nasa.gov/</a> </p>
     <p>Photographes taken by astronauts from International Space Station. There is about 25 000 000 photos. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://eol.jsc.nasa.gov/Info/use.htm">Conditions for Use</a> </p>
     <p><tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<a href="/w/index.php?title=Tag:source%3DImage_courtesy_of_the_Image_Science_%26_Analysis_Laboratory,_NASA_Johnson_Space_Center_-_MissionID-RollID-FrameID&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tag:source=Image courtesy of the Image Science &amp; Analysis Laboratory, NASA Johnson Space Center - MissionID-RollID-FrameID (page does not exist)"><bdi>Image courtesy of the Image Science &amp; Analysis Laboratory, NASA Johnson Space Center - MissionID-RollID-FrameID</bdi></a></tt> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Dept._of_State.2C_International_Boundaries">US Dept. of State, International Boundaries</span></h3> 
     <p>From the Office of the Geographer and Global Issues (INR/GGI), we are free to use these international boundary lines (attribute = 1), other lines of international separation (disputed lines; attribute = 3) and other lines of separation (attribute = 7.) They reflect US govt. policy and thus not necessarily de facto control. This data set is in the public domain; no restrictions on its use. </p>
     <p>The most recent edition (December 2015: "LSIB6b") is available at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.data.gov/">http://www.data.gov/</a> by searching for <i>large scale international boundaries</i>. </p>
     <p><br> The lines are produced and regularly updated by geographers at State and colleagues from other agencies based on imagery, old treaties/maps, and other sources. For most of Europe and the U.S., the lines are not particularly accurate; accurate data for these areas are widely available via other sources. This "Large Scale International Boundary (LSIB)" line data as well as polygons are also available at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://geocommons.com/search?model=&amp;query=LSIB">http://geocommons.com/search?model=&amp;query=LSIB</a>, though there may be some issues with the processing in GeoCommons. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GLIMS_Glacier_Database">GLIMS Glacier Database</span></h3> 
     <p><i>Main page <a href="/wiki/GLIMS_Glacier_Database" title="GLIMS Glacier Database">GLIMS Glacier Database</a></i> </p>
     <p>A database of glacier outlines with a global (although incomplete) coverage. </p>
     <p>Hosted and maintained by the NSIDC, licensed as public domain. </p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Charge_Map">Open Charge Map</span></h3> 
     <p>This is a worldwide database of electric vehicle charging stations. It is mostly open source but with some imported data from third-parties but the data is segregated. It has about 27,000 locations currently listed. The data is mostly community sourced and maintained. </p>
     <p>See <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openchargemap.org">OCM Web Site</a> </p>
     <p>See <a href="/wiki/Open_Charge_Map" class="mw-redirect" title="Open Charge Map">Open Charge Map</a> for further details. </p>
     <p><br> </p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IDERA_.28Spatial_Data_Infrastructure_of_the_Argentinian_Republic.29">IDERA (Spatial Data Infrastructure of the Argentinian Republic)</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.idera.gob.ar/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=64&amp;Itemid=301">Visualizator</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IGN_.28National_Geographic_Institute.29">IGN (National Geographic Institute)</span></h4> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="MAPEAR_.28Unfree.29">MAPEAR (Unfree)</span></h4> 
     <p>Nothing in the project <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.proyectomapear.com.ar/index.php">MAPEAR</a> should be used since their license is not compatible. Although their maps are free as in beer they are not free as in speech. </p> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="geoland.at">geoland.at</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.geoland.at">geoland.at</a> is an effort to bundle GIS data from the Bundesländer (federal states). They state <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.geoland.at/index.php?option=com_content&amp;task=view&amp;id=19&amp;Itemid=51&amp;lang=de">[6]</a> that usage of graphics/information within the scope of publications / websites is only permitted provided that the "© Geoland" and the source reference <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.geoland.at">www.geoland.at</a> are given. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="geoimage.at">geoimage.at</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.geoimage.at">geoimage.at</a> provides a free WMS for whole Austria since October 2010 in 1m resolution (for the time being, they will provide it for the duration of 2 years). Details of the legal situation are still to be worked out, but employees of geoimage.at said, that they definitely are willing to cooperate with OpenStreetMap. Please note, that the WMS is in a special Lambert-projection and (until now) cannot be directly used in any editor without having changed some settings. See <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_Austria/geoimage.at" title="WikiProject Austria/geoimage.at">WikiProject_Austria/geoimage.at</a> for details. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vienna">Vienna</span></h4> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.wien.gv.at/katalog/basiskarten/">Wien.gv.at Open Data</a> - basic maps <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Wien#Useful_Resources_.2F_Ressourcen_f.C3.BCr_Mapper">How to use in JOSM (German)</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.wien.gv.at/katalog/verkehr/">Wien.gv.at Open Data</a> - traffic</li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://offener.datenkatalog.at/package/geokoordinaten-ubahn-stationen-wien">Vienna Subway Stations</a></li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.data.gv.at/katalog/dataset/5349b414-5069-45be-8869-7d94261d4936/">Wien.gv.at Open Data</a> - Vienna Dropped Kerbs point data</li>
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Austria">Upper Austria</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.linz.gv.at/daten/Geodaten/">Linz Open Data</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Styria">Styria</span></h4> 
     <p>The local government of Styria provides GIS data on their website <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.gis.steiermark.at/">[7]</a>. According to the website the data available for download is freely usable "frei verwendbar" (free as in speech) provided their copyright notice "Quelle: GIS-Steiermark" (which would translate to: "Source: GIS-Styria") is preserved. The data covers roads, rivers, cities and political territories. It is available in EsriShape format. Maybe the government of Styria would be willing to relicense their data under CC terms. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="OpenAddresses.at">OpenAddresses.at</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.openaddresses.at/">OpenAddresses.at</a> was a crowd-based effort to collect geo-referenced address data in Austria. It seems to no longer exist but was originally a database available for download under an open license. An <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://karrie.info/projekte/oa2osm/">oa2osm</a> script was created to convert the data for import. </p> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span></h3> 
     <p><i>see also <a href="/wiki/Australian_Data_Imports" title="Australian Data Imports">Australian Data Imports</a></i> </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a href="/wiki/Old_Australia_maps" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Australia maps">Old Australia maps</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ACT_-_GDA94.2FAHD.29_.28Unfree.29">ACT - GDA94/AHD) (Unfree)</span></h4> 
     <p>This only covers the ACT (Australian Capital Territory), which is only a few 100km sq. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ga.gov.au/nmd/products/digidat/100k.htm">http://www.ga.gov.au/nmd/products/digidat/100k.htm</a> </p>
     <p>Currency: 2005. </p>
     <p>Coordinates: Geographical. </p>
     <p>Datum: Geocentric Datum of Australia (GDA94), Australian Height Datum (AHD). </p>
     <p>Format: ESRI Personal Geodatabase Version 8.3, ESRI Shapefile, MapInfo mid/mif and ER Mapper Compressed Wavelet (ECW) Raster. </p>
     <p>Medium: Online Download (free) or Packaged CD-ROM ($99). </p> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="AGIV">AGIV</span></h4> 
     <p>The AGIV (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.agiv.be/gis/nieuws/?artid=2179">http://www.agiv.be/gis/nieuws/?artid=2179</a>) has released some part of its data using the 'Gratis Open Data Licentie Vlaanderen'. We need to mention AGIV as a source on this wiki. </p>
     <p>Some of the data from AGIV that was released in some form as open data: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> CRAB: Addressing database of the Flanders part of Belgium.</li> 
      <li> Orthophotos: Areal imagery; usage of this areal imagery has been confirmed: This is allowed in OpenStreetMap.</li>
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Atlas_de_Buurtwegen">Atlas de Buurtwegen</span></h4> 
     <p>The provinces of West-Vlaanderen, Oost-Vlaanderen, Vlaams-Brabant, Limburg and Antwerpen provide 'De Atlas der buurtwegen' under the terms of the 'Gratis Open Data Licentie Vlaanderen'. </p> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bosnia_and_Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> has made 1:50000 topographical maps of Balkan peninsula countries. These maps are US Federal Government works and are in the public domain in the USA (see copyright statement here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/faq.html#3.html">[8]</a>) and probably in most other countries of the world. The maps are provided as PDF-files from The University of Texas Libraries <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.lib.utexas.edu/maps/topo/former_yugoslavia/">here</a>. Not all maps have been scanned so far, but at least significant parts of the Former Yugoslavian countries, Albania, Bosnia and Herzegovina, Croatia, Kosovo, Montenegro, Macedonia, Serbia and Slovenia are available (coverage: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://osm-hr.org/ustopo.htm">[9]</a>). </p>
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_Croatia" title="WikiProject Croatia">WikiProject Croatia</a> (osm-hr) project have converted the PDF-files in the slippy map format such that the maps can easily be used as backgrounds in JOSM or Potlatch 2. Be careful since some parts of the maps are old and might also have a significant wrong offset. </p>
     <p>JOSM: Go to Edit, Preferences, WMS TMS. Add a TMS-source and specify the URL: <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://tms.osm-hr.org/1.0.0/all_ustopo/{zoom}/{x}/{y}.png">http://tms.osm-hr.org/1.0.0/all_ustopo/{zoom}/{x}/{y}.png</a></code> </p>
     <p>Potlatch 2: Go to Background, Edit and insert the line: <code><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://tms.osm-hr.org/1.0.0/all_ustopo/$z/$x/$y.png">http://tms.osm-hr.org/1.0.0/all_ustopo/$z/$x/$y.png</a></code> </p>
     <p>Thanks to Janko for posting this information (<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://forum.openstreetmap.org/viewtopic.php?pid=220608">[10]</a>), to dodobas for geocoding the PDFs, to hbogner at the Faculty of Geodesy in Zagreb and of course to the US Federal government for creating the maps! </p> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suitable_sources">Suitable sources</span></h4> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ibge.gov.br/mapas/">IBGE</a> Stated to be public domain data <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/imports/2013-July/001981.html">[11]</a>, although it requires citing the source (which can be done as <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<a href="/wiki/Tag:source%3DIBGE" class="mw-redirect" title="Tag:source=IBGE"><bdi>IBGE</bdi></a></tt>)</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.geominas.mg.gov.br/">Projeto Geominas</a> (dead link) Public domain data (citation needed) on Minas Gerais state. Created by the state government, includes geographical, administrative and climatic data.</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aguasparana.pr.gov.br/modules/conteudo/conteudo.php?conteudo=79">Águas Paraná</a> Created by the state of Paraná this data is allowed to use (citation needed) if it's tagged with <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<a href="/w/index.php?title=Tag:source%3D%C3%81guas_Paran%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tag:source=Águas Paraná (page does not exist)"><bdi>Águas Paraná</bdi></a></tt></li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dnit.gov.br/mapas-multimodais/shapefiles">DNIT</a> Confirmed to be PD by email, citation needed, <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<a href="/wiki/Tag:source%3DDNIT" class="mw-redirect" title="Tag:source=DNIT"><bdi>DNIT</bdi></a></tt></li>
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncertain_sources">Uncertain sources</span></h4> 
     <ul>
      <li> Other public and governmental sources - Much of the geographical and statistical data from Federal, state and municipal sources is believed to be under public domain, although no law affirms that (see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikip%C3%A9dia:Recursos_livres#Recursos_governamentais">Wikipédia</a>). One possibility is to proceed on a case-by-case basis: to contact any potential sources, inform about OSM, and ask directly for a statement as to whether the data is free/open/PD.</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> Any other map or source available under unknown licensing terms.</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.uff.br/geoden/docs/GeoLISTA.pdf">GeoLISTA</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Unsuitable_sources">Unsuitable sources</span></h4> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a href="/wiki/Tracksource" title="Tracksource">Tracksource</a> (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tracksource.org.br/index.php?index">tracksource.org.br</a> - Released under CC-BY-NC-ND, therefore incompatible with OSM license due to restrictive distribution for commercial proposes as well as for derivative works. See the bottom of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tracksource.org.br/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=23&amp;Itemid=45">TrackSource about page</a>.</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> Any other map or source available under restrictive licenses.</li>
     </ul> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal">Federal</span></h4> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Geobase">Geobase</span></h5> 
     <p><i>Please see <a href="/wiki/GeoBase_Import" title="GeoBase Import">GeoBase Import</a> as it has been approved for use.</i>--<a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Acrosscanadatrails&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Acrosscanadatrails (page does not exist)">acrosscanadatrails</a> 08:31, 3 December 2008 (UTC) </p>
     <p>Data is free and unrestricted, however, registration is required to download. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>The Geobase web site does claim that the data is free and unrestricted, however, their license still imposes restrictions. See [<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://geobase.ca/geobase/en/licence.jsp">Geobase license</a>] especially sections 4.4 and 6.3 This license when last discussed on the talk mailing list was found to be incompatible with OSMs license. <a href="/wiki/User:Rw" title="User:Rw">Rw</a> 21:08, 12 February 2007 (UTC)</li> 
      <li>I will not upload any more data until I've clarified this, if anyone so wishes feel free to remove the NU data (it fits exclusively inside a 'square'). On my initial, and admittedly brief, review of the GeoBase license, 4.* is purely about indemnifying Canada from liability (a topic Attribution-ShareAlike 2.0 does not seem to cover) while I agree that more clarification of 6.3 would be helpful (it could potentially be argued that OSM is a derivative product under 1.4 and also that under 6.1, 6.* can only lead to termination due to actions on the part of the Licensee - Canada can not revoke the license if, as it stands, it is complied to when the data is taken), having said this I'm not OSM's lawyer. I will contact Natural Resources Canada and see what their take on license compatibility is - would this be sufficient? If possible, could you point me towards the talk mailing list discussion on the issue, so that I'm not repeating what has already been researched.</li> 
      <li>Natural Resources Canada can not evaluate license compatibility due to the potential liability issues that would create for them, so it's back to the data not being usable in it's current state. I will try and get some legal advice on the matter when I'm back in Canada in the fall.</li> 
      <li>I (DShpak) am currently trying to establish a discussion with Geobase about the OpenStreetMap project, and the possibility of granting the data to OSM under a non-attribution licence. <a href="/wiki/User:Dshpak" title="User:Dshpak">Dshpak</a> 18:52, 14 May 2007 (BST)</li> 
      <li>the conversation with Natural Resources Canada has continued. Their most recent email indicating their wish that we use the data and their evaluation that the licenses were compatible. Casual discussion with those on the foundation has been positive but we await an official statement. <a href="/wiki/User:Rw" title="User:Rw">Rw</a> 01:07, 16 July 2008 (UTC)</li> 
      <li>see <a href="/wiki/GeoBase_Import" title="GeoBase Import">GeoBase_Import</a> <a href="/wiki/User:Rw" title="User:Rw">Rw</a> 16:40, 18 November 2008 (UTC)</li>
     </ul> 
     <p>Formats available: </p>
     <p>ESRI Shapefile - same as TIGER, so potentially import scripts could be reused </p>
     <p>Geography Markup Language (GML) </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.geobase.ca/geobase/en/search.do?produit=nrnc1&amp;language=en">http://www.geobase.ca/geobase/en/search.do?produit=nrnc1&amp;language=en</a> </p>
     <p>GeoBase is a federal, provincial and territorial government initiative that is overseen by the Canadian Council on Geomatics (CCOG). Through the GeoBase portal, users with an interest in the field of geomatics have access to quality geospatial information at no cost and with unrestricted use. </p>
     <p><br> On February 11, 2007 the GML file for Nunavut was converted to OSM (using a Visual Studio 2005 C# app from <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.in7ane.com/osm/">http://www.in7ane.com/osm/</a> which so far just extracts/saves ways with road number/name and type metadata) and attempted to be uploaded via JOSM, but repeatedly failed due to timeouts. The source and the converted file are at the above link as well. Splitting into chunks of 5000 nodes seems to work: 1st of 5 Nunavut files seems to have uploaded and rendered ok (<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.informationfreeway.org/?lat=10309654.4095&amp;lon=-7112655.03296&amp;zoom=12&amp;layers=B00">http://www.informationfreeway.org/?lat=10309654.4095&amp;lon=-7112655.03296&amp;zoom=12&amp;layers=B00</a>), so the rest of the Nunavut set was uploaded on February 12, 2007 (4th file timed out on uploading ways, but seemed to resume). </p> 
     <pre>Processed: BC* MB NB NL NS* NT NU PE YT
Uploaded:  NU
*no single osm
</pre> 
     <p>I'm wondering if anyone has any suggestions on A) submitting the large resulting files without having to split them up and submit dozens of files through JOSM B) submitting data for provinces that already have partial road data. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="CanVec">CanVec</span></h5> 
     <p>Please see <a href="/wiki/Canvec" class="mw-redirect" title="Canvec">canvec</a> for details. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="GeoGratis">GeoGratis</span></h5> 
     <p>data: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://geogratis.cgdi.gc.ca/geogratis/en/download/index.html">http://geogratis.cgdi.gc.ca/geogratis/en/download/index.html</a> </p>
     <p>Vector and raster data, including scanned and vector topographic maps, aerial and satellite imagery. </p>
     <p>licence: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://geogratis.cgdi.gc.ca/geogratis/en/licence.jsp">http://geogratis.cgdi.gc.ca/geogratis/en/licence.jsp</a> </p>
     <p>Has the same (as far as a cursory examination suggests) licence as Geobase (above). </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_Canada_.28Unfree.29">Statistics Canada (Unfree)</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://geodepot.statcan.ca/Diss2006/DataProducts/RNF2006_e.jsp">http://geodepot.statcan.ca/Diss2006/DataProducts/RNF2006_e.jsp</a> is the 2006 Road Network File </p>
     <p>Has ARC/INFO, MapInfo, and GML road network data with street names and address ranges (like TIGER/Line data, who they say they are cooperating with). Their license agreement is similar to GeoBase's (they state that their data will become part of GeoBase by the 2011 census), however the data seems to be a bit off from the GeoBase set. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>If they are working on interoperability with TIGER/Line data, which I assume is ok to use in OSM, it would suggest that the data should be ok to use once the license is clarified. (Feb 22 update: waiting for a concrete reply from National Resources Canada about the GeoData license).</li>
     </ul>

     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Trans_Canada_Trail_.28unfree_unconfirmed.29">Trans Canada Trail (unfree unconfirmed)</span></h5> 
     <ul>
      <li> The data is available as a GPX file set, 1 for each province. See <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trans_Canada_Trail&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trans Canada Trail (page does not exist)">Trans Canada Trail</a> for the details.</li> 
      <li> The data was acquired using GPS, BUT acquired by different people and collected and viewed on Google Earth. (So it's not possible to tell the authenticity of the data.) (no vertical profile on GPX data)</li> 
      <li> The <a class="external text" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/relation/146855">sample area</a> was traced with no other user traces, and the <a class="external text" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/relation/146837">other sample</a> was based on actual (my GPS tracks)</li> 
      <li> As long as 'source=trans canada trail' is used it should be fine, but verification with a letter is needed.</li>
     </ul> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_GIS_Consortium_.28Unfree_-_unconfirmed.29">Open GIS Consortium (Unfree - unconfirmed)</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://atlas.nrcan.gc.ca/site/english/dataservices/web_map_service.html">http://atlas.nrcan.gc.ca/site/english/dataservices/web_map_service.html</a> </p>
     <p>I stumbled upon this while looking on Google for WMS data for Canada. It seems to be open, somehow, but I haven't found the explicit license. I also haven't been able to use the WMS server at all.. </p> 
     <dl>
