     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span></h3> 
     <p>Colombia passed an Open Data law in 2014, and since then some cities have made some really useful stuff available. Some of that is CC-By-SA, though, so we'll have to get permission to use it under the ODBL. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ideca.gov.co/es/servicios/mapa-de-referencia/tabla-mapa-referencia?tid_1=All&amp;title=">SHP files including all of the buildings of Bogotá</a>, with number of floors for each part - perfect for <a href="/wiki/3D" title="3D">3D</a>.</li> 
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.datos.gov.co/Ordenamiento-Territorial/UAECD-Predio-2016/wjm3-4xf3">CSV with addresses and usage codes for all the buildings of Bogotá</a>, with codes that we can use to correlate with the above data.</li> 
      <li> Open Data Law (Spanish): <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wsp.presidencia.gov.co/Normativa/Leyes/Documents/LEY%201712%20DEL%2006%20DE%20MARZO%20DE%202014.pdf">PDF</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <hr> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="TMC_LocationTables">TMC LocationTables</span></h4> 
     <p>The national LocationCodeLists of the <a href="/wiki/TMC" title="TMC">TMC</a> (Traffic Message System = traffic-jam warning via radio) -system contain a highly simplified road-network of all the major roads and many important points in the country. The location-codes themself are also highly useful to have in OSM for <a href="/wiki/Routing" title="Routing">Routing</a> -software that can receive TMC-messages and thus avoid traffic jams and other obstructions. </p>
     <p>These lists are sometimes free to use, sometimes closed but due to the fact that they are widely distributed with all commercial navigation-systems, there may be little resistance in getting a permission to tag existing OSM-objects with their location-code or use the list to check for missing ways in our map. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Environment_Agency_.28EEA.29">European Environment Agency (EEA)</span></h4> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/European_Environment_Agency" title="European Environment Agency">European Environment Agency</a> offers data for commercial reuse. Here are potential GIS vector data to be imported: </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Nationally_designated_areas_.28CDDA.29">Nationally designated areas (CDDA)</span></h5> 
     <p>This is about nature conservation - protected areas: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li>national parks</li> 
      <li>nature parks</li> 
      <li>etc.</li>
     </ul> 
     <p>A <a href="/wiki/Shapefile" class="mw-redirect" title="Shapefile">shapefile</a> is provided with latest data of 2011: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eea.europa.eu/data-and-maps/data/nationally-designated-areas-national-cdda-5">CDDA_v9_polygons.zip</a> </p>
     <p><br> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Via_Alpina_dataset_on_accommodation_in_the_Alps">Via Alpina dataset on accommodation in the Alps</span></h4> 
     <p>See <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/File:Authorisation_ViaAlpina_OSM_accomodation.png">http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/File:Authorisation_ViaAlpina_OSM_accomodation.png</a> </p>
     <p>638 accommodation places, many attributes. Dataset in 5 languages. Example: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.via-alpina.org/point/1598">http://www.via-alpina.org/point/1598</a> </p>
     <p>The origin (licence) and accuracy of the location is uncertain, so better to use the attributes only. Part of the data is already outdated, so it is advised to check first (maybe by calling). In Italy at least, the '0' (zero) after +39 is missing in the online phone numbers (but GSM lines do not have zeroes). </p>
     <p>(Do not hesitate to contact me or the Via Alpina international secretary for more details <a href="/wiki/User:Mayeul" title="User:Mayeul">Mayeul</a> 18:03, 31 May 2012 (BST)) </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Maastotietokanta">Maastotietokanta</span></h4> 
     <p>The National Land Survey of Finland (NLS) has recently (1 May 2012) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.maanmittauslaitos.fi/en/node/6567">opened</a> some of its dataset under an attribution only -licence. The amount of data available is enormous, and the local community is discussing the details. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="digiroad">digiroad</span></h4> 
     <p>The Finnish Road Administration (Tiehallinto) maintains a database called <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.digiroad.fi">digiroad</a> covering all roads and streets in Finland which would contain all information OpenStreetMap needs about roads for Finland. (Shorelines, parks, amenities, boundaries, placenames, etc would still have to be collected using traditional OSM procedures.) The database is available for licensing relatively cheap, a few hundred euro. Unfortunately, as far as I can see, it is not currently licensed under terms suitable for OpenStreetMap. The English summary document says that "Data from Digiroad will be free-of-charge for public organisations for internal use and for free public services" but I couldn't find anything as promising in the more recent Finnish documentation. </p>
     <p>However, my (naïve?) hope is that it will eventually be possible to convince them to "open up" the data enough for OpenStreetMap. Clearly digiroad is not maintained and sold for profit, there aren't even any royalty fees collected from commercial users of the data. </p>
     <p>I mailed the project coordinator asking for more information. The coordinator had changed from that mentioned on their webpage to another person though, though, but I did eventually get a reply from her. Basically it was quite positive, but they need time to consider this. They also interpret current regulations as allowing them to sell (for the very reasonable amount) the material only to companies and institutions, not to individuals. Also the data should be used to benefit "services for transport and logistics" (badly translated from the vague term "liikkumisen palvelut"), but on the other hand, what else could it be used for? (Maybe the intent of this restriction is to prevent production of pure maps from the data. That would then indeed seriously prevent importing it into OSM, I think.) </p>
     <p>I sent more mail asking for clarifications, pointing out that the price as such is not the issue here, surely it would be possible to collect for instance 20 euros per person from a group of interested individuals, or even ask some company to "sponsor" freeing this data. The licensing issues are the main concern. No further replies yet. </p>
     <p>I hacked together some code to convert the sample data available from the website <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.digiroad.fi/files/fi_FI/esimerkkiaineistot/">[15]</a> (sorry, documentation in Finnish and Swedish only) into OSM format. See here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.iki.fi/tml/digiroad2osm.c">[16]</a>. Plain C. Needs shapelib and iconv(), otherwise no external dependencies. Screenshot of part of sample data loaded into JOSM here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.iki.fi/tml/sshot1.png">[17]</a>. </p>
     <p>--<a href="/wiki/User:Tml" title="User:Tml">Tml</a> 09:33, 24 September 2007 (BST) </p>
     <p>The Finnish page says that the licensing conditions are formed to match client requirements so it should be possible to get a good license. Then the only problem would be their fee (about €380) which mandated by law. --<a href="/wiki/User:LH" title="User:LH">LH</a> 15:11, 9 September 2007 (BST) </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
        No fee anymore for Digiroad, and data is available currently from FTP server (need to request access still, though), and should be available from some "downloading service" by the end of this year. --
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Vessep&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Vessep (page does not exist)">Vessep</a> (
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=User_talk:Vessep&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User talk:Vessep (page does not exist)">talk</a>) 09:25, 16 September 2014 (UTC)
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <dl>
        <dd>
          Download service now open 
         <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://extranet.liikennevirasto.fi/extranet/web/public/latauspalvelu">here</a>, in Finnish only --
         <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Vessep&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Vessep (page does not exist)">Vessep</a> (
         <a href="/w/index.php?title=User_talk:Vessep&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User talk:Vessep (page does not exist)">talk</a>) 06:44, 29 September 2014 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl>
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <p><i>Reading the contract details, the licence gives you the right to use the data for a certain purpose for a maximum of 5 years. After the 5 year period the copy must be returned or destroyed. I recommend reading the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.digiroad.fi/Tilaus/fi_FI/tilaus_1/_files/11233325660000233/default/sopimusluonnos.pdf">example contract</a>.</i> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="RHK">RHK</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rhk.fi">The Finnish Rail Administration</a> possibly has exact geodata for all of the state-owned rail network. With rail deregulation being implemented and all, they seem to be quite open, and publish lots of information on the web, including a very detailled "Network Statement". Alas, this document doesn't include coordinates of stations etc, only the distance (down to one metre resolution) along the rails from the designated point of origin. (Trivia: this point of origin is the previous Helsinki station, 159m south of the present Helsinki Central station, and not actually accessible by rail.) I mailed then asking if the network geodata (and useful other information, like number of tracks and electrification) could be made available in some suitable format and could be donated to OSM. They didn't promise anything except that maybe in the next "Network Statement" they will include actual coordinates. So probably it doesn't make sense to wait for something that might not happen, but continue mapping rail lines as before. </p>
     <p>They have an interactive web service that contains information for all <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tasoristeys.fi/">level crossings</a> in Finland. For many of the crossings coordinates are included (in the Finnish national KKJ grid, not WGS84, but conversion formulae are well-known) . From this service one could semi-mechanically generate an at least partially quite accurate (for those lines that have plenty of level crossings) map of the rail network. This might be interesting especially for freight-only lines where actual GPS mapping of course is hard to do (without actually trekking along the line). Data for one level crossing here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.tasoristeys.fi/risteyshaku?crossingId=3167">[18]</a>. Their reply to my mail was a bit vague but I got the impression that it should be OK to import the level crossing locations. The location of an individual crossing is obviously not a copyrightable work, but as a collection it is covered by copyright for databases and collections. </p>
     <p>--<a href="/wiki/User:Tml" title="User:Tml">Tml</a> 08:28, 25 October 2007 (BST) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_of_Tampere">City of Tampere</span></h4> 
     <p>The City of Tampere has <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tampere.fi/tampereinfo/avoindata.html">published a number of datasets</a> (and plans to publish more) under an <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tampere.fi/tampereinfo/avoindata/avoindatalisenssi.html">attribution-only license</a> which might be compatible with our license. If it's not, they just might relicense the data for us under ODbL if we ask nicely. </p>
     <p>Data that might be relevant here includes bus routes, bus stop locations, hiking paths, pier locations, statistical data and zoning area boundaries. </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
       <dl>
        <dd>
         Addendum: This license is very similar to the MML (NLS) open data license, except instead of a share-alike provision, there is only an attribution provision - which may mean 
         <small>(disclaimer: IANAL)</small> the data can be relicensed under ODbL. —
         <a href="/w/index.php?title=User:Joemppe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="User:Joemppe (page does not exist)">Joemppe</a> 00:11, 28 December 2012 (UTC)
        </dd>
       </dl>
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ODA_Self_care_and_digital_value_services">ODA Self care and digital value services</span></h4> 
     <p>The Finnish National Institute for Health and Welfare (THL) maintains a registry for all public and private social and health care providers. The registry includes various information about the providers, such as their name and address. Interesting is also the type of the provider, indicating if the provider is a social services or health services provider, or both. </p>
     <p>From this information one can using geocoding create a set of locations for the registered providers, including their type. Geocoding can be done using the Digitransit service that maintains data on OSM as well. </p>
     <p>The registry is available on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.thl.fi/en/web/information-management-in-social-welfare-and-health-care/standardisation-of-data-and-requirements/code-service">Code Service</a> licensed under CC BY 4.0. Written permission to use the data has been obtained. THL requires an attribution on the copyright page. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span></h3> 
     <p><i>Main article:</i> <a href="/wiki/Potential_Datasources/France" title="Potential Datasources/France">Potential Datasources/France</a> <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_France" title="WikiProject France">France</a> has its <a href="/wiki/Potential_Datasources/France" title="Potential Datasources/France">own page</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span></h3> 
     <p>Germany has its own <a href="/wiki/Datenquellen" class="mw-redirect" title="Datenquellen">wiki page</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span></h3> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://geodata.gov.gr">Geodata</a> is the official governmental site that provides open geospatial data and services for Greece, serving as a national open data catalogue, an INSPIRE-conformant Spatial Data Infrastructure, as well as a powerful foundation for enabling value added services from open data. </p>
     <p>Athens Urban Transport Organisation (AUTO) has released useful information under Creative Commons License (CC BY v.3.0) at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://geodata.gov.gr/en/dataset/oasa">http://geodata.gov.gr/en/dataset/oasa</a> . Data is almost up to date, but it is clearly stated in the context that data is subject to change without any warning or liability of OASA (AUTO), OSY (Road Transportation) or STASY (Railway Transportation). Moreover "the data accuracy is limited, because digitalization hasn't been based on descriptive data". Be aware that real bus stop positions may vary between ±20m. in urban areas and more that 50m. in suburban areas. </p>
     <p>The files available as downloads on this site are in .XML, .shp, .gml &amp; .KML formats. No CSV files are available, you'll have to convert them yourself. The site is in Greek (language) so you'll have to use a translator service to make "lat &amp; long" of the site. Easy enough to navigate if you know what you're looking for, otherwise not a particularly user friendly site. Amendment: OSM requirements are met. </p>
     <p>Another valuable resource site hosting various databases for Greece is <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://datahub.io/group/country-gr?page=1">http://datahub.io/group/country-gr?page=1</a>. A wide range of data-sets are available. Sources are varied, thus the available database file formats differ from set to set. File formats include .CSV, .KML, .XML, .shp, .gml &amp; .ods. Each database has its own license, therefore no comment can be made about OSM requirements. The site is in English (language) &amp; provides an efficient filter for various attributes. A downloading feature is available as is a preview of the relevant file. The original links are available which in most instances are hosted by Greek Government site mentioned earlier. </p>
     <p>A site providing info regarding postcodes in Greece is <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.elta.gr/en-us/findapostcode.aspx">http://www.elta.gr/en-us/findapostcode.aspx</a> . The interface is not very helpful, because it is mainly an address name search engine, but if you are interested for a particular known address, it can precisely give you the corresponding postcode. The English version above accepts transliterated data (Greeklish). However, a native language version is also available at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.elta.gr/el-gr/???????????????.aspx">http://www.elta.gr/el-gr/???????????????.aspx</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honduras">Honduras</span></h3>

     <p>More information in the <a href="/wiki/IT:Potential_Datasources" class="mw-redirect" title="IT:Potential Datasources">Italian page</a>. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Agenzia_del_territorio">Agenzia del territorio</span></h4> 
     <p>Lists containing <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.agenziaterritorio.it/?id=4021#archivi">street-names</a> for all of the italian municipalities, grouped by province, are available for download. For each street-name, the pertaining municipality is identified by its cadastral code (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Codice_catastale">vecchio codice catastale</a>). Check the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.agenziaterritorio.it/sites/territorio/files/servizi/comuni_conservatorie_19-04-2006.pdf">list of italian cadastral codes</a> for interpretation. </p>
     <p>License need to be clarified. Helpful for quality assurance checks. Data might be partly outdated. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Istat">Istat</span></h4> 
     <p>Italian Statistical Institute (ISTAT) has granted to OSM the use of the following data: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.istat.it/ambiente/cartografia/">Administrative Borders</a>: the shapefile provided contain the so called <i>generalized borders</i>, which are a simplified version of the official borders. The version dated 2001 has already been fully imported (more information on a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Italian_Borders">dedicated page</a>). Currently a new version dated 2008/12/31 is available.</li> 
      <li> A list of geographical coordinates of Italian localities. Files and related information are made available by GFOSS from a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://geodati.gfoss.it/wiki/index.php/Dati_liberi_-_Localit%C3%A0_Istat">dedicated page</a>.</li>
     </ul> 
     <p>A <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.istat.it/strumenti/definizioni/comuni/">list of Italian municipalities</a> is also available for download. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portale_Cartografico_Nazionale">Portale Cartografico Nazionale</span></h4> 
     <p>For the whole of Italy there is a WMS server. In 2010 <b>use of 2 WMS-layers for OSM was explicitly permitted (orthographic photos from 2006 for the whole of Italy and from 2008 covering only the regions Lazio and Umbria)</b> (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/File:ITALY_Auth_portale_cartografico_nazionale.png">see authorization letter from the PCN</a>). The rest of the information on the PCN is not free to use for OSM as of May 2010. For more information and instructions how to use the aerial imagery, please visit <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_Italy/PCN" title="WikiProject Italy/PCN">WikiProject_Italy/PCN</a> in Italian language. These photos offer (almost) complete coverage and are much better aligned than Bing aerial, but Bing has higher resolution and is more up to date so if you want to use aerial imagery for mapping in Italy you should probably use both sources. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post">Post</span></h4> 
     <p>A list of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://italy.fsfe.org/it/projects/cap/">Italian postal codes</a> is provided by the Free Software Foundation Europe. It includes the list of street-names for major cities. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regione_Autonoma_Friuli-Venezia-Giulia">Regione Autonoma Friuli-Venezia-Giulia</span></h4> 
     <p>All of the data created and maintained by the Regional Administration </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regione_Lombardia">Regione Lombardia</span></h4> 
     <p>Regione Lombardia has its own <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Lombardia_ToDo">wiki page</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regione_Piemonte">Regione Piemonte</span></h4> 
     <p>The Regione Piemonte has put data from their stock online at <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.dati.piemonte.it/">[19]</a> These include a detailed DEM and the CTRN for the whole of Piemonte down to 1:10000 resolution. Some of the data are quite old, but potentially still extremely useful (e.g. for streams, toponyms). The data are under various CC licenses. No permission to use the data in OSM has yet been requested or given. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Regione_Toscana">Regione Toscana</span></h4> 
     <p>Over 150 layers are available through a public WMS service named <b><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rete.toscana.it/sett/territorio/carto/repertorio/geoscopio_wms/">Geoscopio</a></b>. More details here: <a href="/wiki/Toscana#GEOscopio_WMS" title="Toscana">Toscana#GEOscopio_WMS</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kadena_Air_Base">Kadena Air Base</span></h4> 
     <ul>
      <li> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.kadenafss.com/images/RisnerFitness/Running%20Map%202013.pdf">Running map</a> US Government created</li>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="KSJ">KSJ</span></h4> 
     <p>National-Land Information Office, a section of <i>National and Regional Planning Bureau(NRPB), Ministry of Land, Infrastructure and Transport(MLIT), Japan</i>, provides some geo data. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/ksj/">http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/ksj/</a> </p>
     <p><b>Licenses</b> – <b>IMPORTANT: KSJ IS PROHIBITED TO USE AFTER 2015 DUE TO THEIR LICENSE CHANGE</b> Their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/ksj/other/yakkan.html">terms of use</a> is written in Japanese; a summary in English is as follows. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> 2-3. If you reproduce the National-Land Information or create derivative works, you must do a citation of the source (e.g., "?????????????????????", a literal translation, <i>National-Land Numerical Information (XX Data), MLIT Japan</i>). </li> 
      <li> 3-1. You may use the National-Land Information free of charge.</li> 
      <li> 4. Disclaimer. MLIT Japan makes no warranty on your use of the National-Land Information.</li>
     </ul> 
     <p><b>Accuracy/Quality</b> – Almost National-Land Numerical Information is based on "Map 25000" and "Map 50000" by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gsi.go.jp/ENGLISH/">Geographical Survey Institute (GSI) Japan</a>. Files are in KSJ original format and datum is Japanese Geodetic Datum 2000 (JGD2000) which is based on ITRF94 and GRS80. </p>
     <p>This is the old data of KSJ2 and it have some type of data which KSJ2 doesn't have, e.g. road, submarine cable?and power line, cultural properties, etc. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="KSJ2">KSJ2</span></h4> 
     <p>Their license prohibit to use as business, so we cannot import KSJ2 data source. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/ksj/">http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/ksj/</a> </p>
     <p>National-Land Information Office, a section of <i>National and Regional Planning Bureau(NRPB), Ministry of Land, Infrastructure and Transport(MLIT), Japan</i>, provides some geo data. See <a href="/wiki/Import/Catalogue/Japan_KSJ2_Import" title="Import/Catalogue/Japan KSJ2 Import">KSJ2</a> page. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ISJ">ISJ</span></h4> 
     <p>National-Land Information Office, a section of <i>NRPB, MLIT Japan</i>, provides place reference information in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City_block">city block</a> level for many (not all) municipalities. <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/isj/">http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/isj/</a> </p>
     <p><b>Licenses</b> – Their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nlftp.mlit.go.jp/isj/agreement.html">terms of use</a> is written in Japanese; a summary in English is as follows. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> 2-3. If you reproduce the place reference information or create derivative works, you must do a citation of the source (e.g., "???????????????????", a literal translation, <i>City Block Level Place Reference Information, MLIT Japan</i>). </li> 
      <li> 3-1. You may use the place reference information free of charge.</li> 
      <li> 4. Disclaimer. MLIT Japan makes no warranty on your use of the place reference information.</li>
     </ul> 
     <p><b>Accuracy/Quality</b> – Place reference information is based on "Numerical Map 2500" by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gsi.go.jp/ENGLISH/">Geographical Survey Institute (GSI) Japan</a>. Files are in CSV(Comma Separated Values) format, SHIFT-JIS encoding and datum is Japanese Geodetic Datum 2000 (JGD2000) which is based on ITRF94 and GRS80. </p>
     <p>I guess we can use this data like CC-BY/CC-BY-SA data as imported before. -- <a href="/wiki/User:Tatata" title="User:Tatata">Tatata</a> 10:52, 25 February 2008 (UTC) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthophoto_.28MLIT_Japan.29">Orthophoto (MLIT Japan)</span></h4> 
     <p>National-Land Information Office, a section of <i>NRPB, MLIT Japan</i>, provides aerial photography for old survey with WMS. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://orthophoto.mlit.go.jp/">Web (Japanese only)</a> </p>
     <p><b>Licenses</b> – Their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://orthophoto.mlit.go.jp/ols_doc4.html">terms of use</a> is written in Japanese; a summary in English is as follows. </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> 2. <b>Notices</b> 
       <ul>
        <li> 3. If you republish the data or create derivative works, you must do a citation of the source (e.g., "????????????????????????", a literal translation, <i>National Land Imaginary Information (Orthophoto), MLIT Japan</i>). Recode information of the photograph's taken date, digitized date and the file name, and editors' names as long as possible.</li>
       </ul></li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> 3. <b>availability</b> 
       <ol>
        <li> Anyone is allowed to use national land information by free for charge, except fees for communication, etc.</li> 
        <li> Read well this term of use. You needed to agree this term of use before you use it.</li> 
        <li> If you use this information, you are regarded to agree the term of use.</li>
       </ol></li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> 4. <b>Disclaimer</b> 
       <ul>
        <li> MLIT Japan makes no warranty on your use of the place reference information.</li>
       </ul></li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> 5. <b>Notes</b> 
       <ul>
        <li> This term of use could be changed without any notices.</li>
       </ul></li>
     </ul> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/User:Ikiya" title="User:Ikiya">User:ikiya</a> confirmed to the office that we can use the aerial photography to draw our map with the following annotations <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-ja/2009-November/001880.html">[20]</a>: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source:ja" class="mw-redirect" title="Key:source:ja">source:ja</a></bdi>=<bdi>?????????????????????</bdi></tt></li> 
      <li> <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:source" title="Key:source">source</a></bdi>=<bdi>MLIT Japan</bdi></tt></li>
     </ul> 
     <p>The URL of WMS: </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd> 
       <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://orthophoto.mlit.go.jp:8888/wms/service/wmsRasterTileMap?SERVICE=WMS&amp;REQUEST=GetCapabilities">http://orthophoto.mlit.go.jp:8888/wms/service/wmsRasterTileMap?SERVICE=WMS&amp;REQUEST=GetCapabilities</a>
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <p>We have got another confirmation for the first and the second derivative works form the orthophotos.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-ja/2009-December/002058.html">[21]</a> OpenStreetMap data directly generated from the orthophotos must show "?????????????????????" in the data browser of www.openstreetmap.org. The source tag is useful for it. Then, for the second derivative works, which means works derived form OpenStreetMap data, must show "(C) OpenStreetMap" and make a web link to <a class="external free" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/">http://www.openstreetmap.org/</a> . That is the same with <a href="/wiki/OpenStreetMap_License" title="OpenStreetMap License">Our License</a>. </p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Data_Catalog_Shizuoka">Open Data Catalog Shizuoka</span></h4>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/INEGI" title="INEGI">INEGI</a> (Instituto Nacional de Estadística y Geografía) </p>
     <p>On september 2014 it was officially released the Normative for Open Data published by INEGI (Mexico’s Equivalent of USGS+US Census Bureau, or Brazil’s IBGE). </p>
     <p>The release was published in the Official Gazette of the Federation, which is the main official government publication in Mexico. The importance of this is that the main rules and regulations of the three branches of the federal government are published on this Gazette. It’s a mandate that all official government rules and regulations to be published on it, and so only through this publication that compliance of any law in Mexico becomes mandatory. Once a law or regulation is published on this journal, ignorance of it is no longer a legal defense. </p>
     <p>The terms of use for the information released by INEGI make that information open even for commercial use (with only the requirement of attribution, when technically feasible). This means anyone can use the geographic data released by this institute and import it to OpenStreetMap without incurring on any violation of a license, individuals and companies can use the information for any purpose as long as it follows the terms of use for open data issued by the Mexican government which means they should be released under the following terms: </p>
     <p>Of the Open Data Attributes: I. Public.- Are made public in accordance with the Law of the System; II. Free.- can be obtained without giving any consideration in exchange; III. Nondiscriminatory.- The are accessible without access restriction to users; IV. Free use.- Shall cite the source as the only requirement to be used freely; </p>
     <p>Sources: </p>
     <p>Publication of the National Open Data law (Spanish) <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.dof.gob.mx/nota_detalle.php?codigo=5382838&amp;fecha=20/02/2015">[22]</a> </p>
     <p>Terms of use for open data published on INEGI’s website(Spanish) <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.inegi.org.mx/terminos/terminos_info.aspx">[23]</a> </p>
     <p>Official release statement(Spanish): <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.inegi.org.mx/inegi/contenidos/espanol/prensa/Boletines/Boletin/Comunicados/Especiales/2014/Diciembre/comunica.pdf">[24]</a> </p>
     <p>Publication of the National Geographic Information data law in the Official Gazette of the Federation: (Spanish) <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.dof.gob.mx/nota_detalle.php?codigo=5374183&amp;fecha=04/12/2014">[25]</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.dof.gob.mx/nota_detalle.php?codigo=5374184&amp;fecha=04/12/2014">[26]</a> </p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="TERYT">TERYT</span></h4> 
     <p>TERYT is official government registry of administrative division of Poland. The public data contains names and identifiers for all voivodeships (provinces), powiats (counties), municipalities, places and even streets. </p>
     <p><b>Licenses</b> – public domain </p>
     <p><b>Accuracy/Quality</b> – This is the offical list of places, but it contains no geo location data. May be useful for quality assurance and updating <tt style="background:#EEF" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><bdi style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Key:is_in" title="Key:is in">is_in</a></bdi>=*</tt> tags. More information (in Polish) at <a href="/wiki/WikiProject_Poland/Podzia%C5%82_administracyjny" title="WikiProject Poland/Podzia? administracyjny">WikiProject Poland/Podzia? administracyjny</a> </p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruanda:_Republic_of_Rwanda">Ruanda: Republic of Rwanda</span></h3> 
     <p>Ministry of the Interior and for Sports Rhineland-Palatinate, Germany, has published a 1:300k raster map for whole Ruanda. The right to use the map for OSM was granted by Hanne Hall, Referatsleiterin, Entwicklungszusammenarbeit mit dem Partnerland Ruanda, MINISTERIUM DES INNERN, FÜR SPORT UND INFRASTRUKTUR, Schillerplatz 3-5, 55116 Mainz, Germany, on 20th July 2011. </p> 
     <pre>
20.07.2011 08:41
Betreff: AW: Ruandakarte und openstreetmap.org


Sehr geehrter Herr Keller,

vielen Dank für Ihre Anfrage. Ich habe Ihr Anliegen von der zuständigen Abteilung unseres Hauses klären lassen. Danach spricht
nichts gegen eine Verwendung unseres Kartenmaterials durch Open Street Map. 
Sofern Sie dies also veranlassen möchten, steht dem nichts im Wege.


Mit freundlichen Grüßen
Im Auftrag
-- 
Hanne Hall
Referatsleiterin
Entwicklungszusammenarbeit mit dem Partnerland Ruanda

MINISTERIUM DES INNERN, FÜR SPORT UND INFRASTRUKTUR 

Schillerplatz 3-5

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chief_Directorate:_Surveys_and_Mapping_of_South_Africa">Chief Directorate: Surveys and Mapping of South Africa</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://w3sli.wcape.gov.za/">Chief Directorate: Surveys and Mapping of South Africa</a> has 1:50k raster maps available for the whole of South Africa, these maps are available using the South African <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.info.gov.za/gazette/acts/2000/a2-00.pdf">Freedom of Information Act</a> </p>
     <p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://w3sli.wcape.gov.za/SURVEYS/MAPPING/disclaim.htm">License Agreement</a> is fairly restrictive from OSM's point of view. "No products may be copied or reproduced by any means, including digital, without prior permission." </p>
     <p>"The Licensee shall not Commercialise the Data or any product or service derived from or incorporating the Data, unless it has first obtained the written consent of the CDSM. The CDSM may grant or refuse its consent in its absolute discretion and may grant its consent subject to any condition or conditions whatsoever." </p>
     <p>Recently discussed <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.freeourdata.org.uk/blog/?p=105">here</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.freeourdata.org.uk/blog/?p=106">here</a>. </p> 
     <dl>
      <dd>
        It is uncertain if the data is completely free/libré. Does the "Promotion of Access to Information Act" not grant this? Further investigation is needed.
      </dd>
     </dl> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_Demarcation_Board">Municipal Demarcation Board</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.demarcation.org.za/">Municipal Demarcation Board</a> distributes shapefiles of South African provinces, districts and municipalities. <a href="/wiki/User:Firefishy" title="User:Firefishy">Grant Slater</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk-za/2007-September/000119.html">has received</a> permission to use the data in OpenStreetMap. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="MadMappers_.28Data_Dependent.29">MadMappers (Data Dependent)</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.madmappers.com/">MadMappers</a> seems to have a large amount of data covering the whole of Africa. It may be worth contacting them. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span></h3> 
     <p>See <a href="/wiki/Spain_Potential_Datasources" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain Potential Datasources">Spain Potential Datasources</a> for a more up-to-date information (in Spanish) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="SIGPAC">SIGPAC</span></h4> 
     <p>One branch of the local government has a GIS-like application for controlling the rural land use, with a lot of excellent ortophotos: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://sigpac.mapa.es/fega/visor/">http://sigpac.mapa.es/fega/visor/</a> (Flash required) This branch has been contacted, and they have said (quite literally): </p> 
     <div style="border:1px solid #aaa; margin-left:0.5em; padding:0.5em; overflow:auto"> 
      <pre>[We] have no problem in the images of the SIGPAC being used in [the OpenStreetMap] project.
</pre> 
     </div> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="IDEE">IDEE</span></h4> 
     <p>People from Madrid have already contacted the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ign.es">IGN</a> ("Instituto Geográfico Nacional" or "National Geographic Institute"). They want to make data "more public", and so have agreed to let us import some of their data. Depending on the success and impact, we might be able to import lots of data and use the new aerial imagery (called "PNOA", covering the entire country at 50 cm/px). </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cadastrial_data">Cadastrial data</span></h4> 
     <p>Spanish Cadastre is publishing all cadastrial data as a WMS service <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.catastro.meh.es/esp/servicios_destacados1.asp#menu5">[28]</a>. They say: </p> 
     <div style="border:1px solid #aaa; margin-left:0.5em; padding:0.5em; overflow:auto"> 
      <pre>La Dirección General del Catastro ofrece como servicio WMS la Cartografía Catastral de forma libre y gratuita.
"The general directorate of the cadastre offers the Cadastrial Cartography as a WMS service, free** and free*"
</pre> 
     </div> 
     <p>* as in "free beer" </p>
     <p>** as in "freedom" </p>
     <p>Cadastrial data can also be downloaded from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www1.sedecatastro.gob.es/">Official site</a> as shapefiles (cartography) and *.CAT files (alphanumeric information). Terms of use are regulated by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.catastro.meh.es/documentos/normativa/res_230311.pdf">Resolución de 23 de marzo de 2011, de la Dirección General del Catastro, por la que se aprueban los criterios de acceso, formatos de entrega y condiciones de la licencia-tipo para el acceso al servicio de descarga masiva de datos y cartografía, a través de la Sede Electrónica del Catastro.</a> which states: </p> 
     <div style="border:1px solid #aaa; margin-left:0.5em; padding:0.5em; overflow:auto"> 
      <pre>Se autoriza el uso público, incluido el comercial, de la información catastral que haya sido 
sometida a cualquier proceso previo de transformación...

Public use of cadastrial data is permitted, including commercial use, if such data have
been previously transformed in any way...
</pre> 
     </div> 
     <p>According to the above statement, data from Spanish Cadastre can be imported into OSM once it has been transformed, for example from the original shapefiles-&gt;reproyected to EPSG:4326-&gt;converted to *.osm format. </p>
     <p>Spanish Cadastre has a lot of information with very high accuracy, such as buildings (shape, use, height, number of floors, etc.), land use, most of streets and roads of the country, power station, trees... Many of this information is currently in OSM, mainly ways and roads, but a great part is missing, especially in low populated areas where a ground survey is less likely to be made. More information about this topic can be found in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Cadastre" title="Spanish Cadastre"> Catastro España</a>. A long discussion has been held on <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/wiki/Talk-es">Spanish mailing list</a>, with general agreement on the usefulness of importing these data. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthoimaginery">Orthoimaginery</span></h4> 
     <p>The IGN publishes a lot of (free as in "free beer") imaginery at <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.ign.es/ign_iberpix/index.htm">[29]</a> </p>
     <p>Besides that, there is a list of available orthoimaginery sources at <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.hispacad.com/foro/viewtopic.php?t=4029&amp;postdays=0&amp;postorder=asc&amp;start=15">[30]</a> </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lantm.C3.A4teriet">Lantmäteriet</span></h4> 
     <p>The official Swedish road map, terrain map and mountain map have been released under CC-BY 4.0. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Valmyndigheten">Valmyndigheten</span></h4> 
     <p>The Swedish Election Authority. They provide zip files of GIS-data with shapes. Swedish description: Filerna är zippade och innehåller shape-filer som visar namn och id på respektive geografisk enhet. Du måste ha speciell GIS-programvara för att se dessa filer. Website: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.val.se/val/val2010/statistik/index.html#gis">[31]</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="NVDB">NVDB</span></h4> 
     <p>Nationell vägdatabas (National Road Database) coordinates road information in Sweden. Website: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.nvdb.se/">[32]</a> or <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.vv.se/nvdb">[33]</a> </p>
     <p>NVDB is a government assignment for Vägverket (Swedish Road Administration). NVDB contains a reference roadmap and additional data. It is used by governmental and private entities. </p>
     <p>License: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.trafikverket.se/tjanster/Oppna_data/">CC-0</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fordonsgas_.28CNG_Natural_Gas_Fuel_Stations.29">Fordonsgas (CNG Natural Gas Fuel Stations)</span></h4> 
     <p>Natural Gas fuel stations are published by Fordonsgas as GPS coordinates on their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fordonsgas.se/Svenska/Tankstallen.aspx">site</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id=".C3.96rebro_city_map_data">Örebro city map data</span></h4> 
     <p>The city of Örebro offers some map data (as GML, JSON and WMS layers). License should be compatible, since it is CC-0. Website: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.orebro.se/8760.html">http://www.orebro.se/8760.html</a> </p>
     <p>Note: You will need to change projection to make the WMS layer work with JOSM. I was only able to get EPSG:3009 to work. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stockholm">Stockholm</span></h4> 
     <p>Open data for Stockholm stad. License is unclear. I have only been able to find some mentions about conforming to opendefinition.org. Didn't say which specific license though. Website: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://open.stockholm.se/oppna-data/geodata/">http://open.stockholm.se/oppna-data/geodata/</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Swedish_County_Administrative_Boards">Swedish County Administrative Boards</span></h4> 
     <p>The Swedish County Administrative Boards offer some map data (as Shape files) and also some metadata related to the GIS data. Website: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://gis.lst.se/lstgis/">[34]</a> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Various">Various</span></h4> 
     <p>There is apparently some sort of competition for innovative uses of open data sources going on this year (2015), this site has a list (in Swedish) of various open data sources and their licenses: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://hackforsweden.se/data/">http://hackforsweden.se/data/</a> </p>
     <p>Not all of them have compatible licenses, and not all of them are geographical data, but there might be some useful data in there. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span></h3> 
     <p>The Swiss-specific datasources are listed on their own <a href="/wiki/Switzerland/Datasources" title="Switzerland/Datasources">Wiki-page</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</span></h3> 
     <p>Tajikistan is at the same time one of the most poorly mapped countries on OSM and a very prone-to-disasters country, thus the need to find good data sources and to improve the quality of the map. A <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajikistan">dedicated Wiki-page</a> page has been setup. </p>
     <p>So far, I haven't found any national dataset that is for sure 100% free of copyrights. Some potential sources are listed below, with mention of the potential problem. Please feel free to contribute to this list: </p> 
     <ul>
      <li> Scanned Soviet maps: although not completely up-to-date, those maps are still widely used in the country (mainly because there's nothing better available). The legal status is unclear (namely: have the copyrights fallen into the public domain with the collapse of the USSR or have they been passed to the Russian Administration? The latter seems to be the opinion of Russian mappers). See on the mailing list: <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://lists.openstreetmap.org/pipermail/talk/2010-June/051194.html">[35]</a></li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> Digitized 1/200000 maps: a vectorized version of the Soviet maps widely circulates in Tajikistan but the license terms are unclear (as they are not distributed with the data itself). Has anyone a crystal-clear and unambiguous proof of the licensing status of this dataset?</li>
     </ul> 
     <ul>
      <li> Any other idea?</li>
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UK">UK</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_authority_street_naming_notifications">Local authority street naming notifications</span></h4> 
     <p>I wrote an email to my local authority when I found out that they notify interested parties on the council's decisions on naming and numbering new properties and streets. For areas that have already been densely surveyed and mapped (90%+), it would be an invaluable list of places that might need re-surveying or other editing. </p>
     <p>I got an answer back - the council <i>do</i> make the information freely available on their web site, but it's in the form of a PDF file per decision, in a human readable format only, and the whole list is not easily searchable. The information contains no geographic information other than relative references, eg. </p> 
     <pre>       That a new development of a house being built on the
       site adjacent to 47 Belmont Avenue, Barnet, Herts, EN4
       shall be postally addressed:
       WOODVIEW HOUSE, 1A NORRYS ROAD, BARNET,
       HERTS, EN4 9JX.
</pre> 
     <p>Occasionally, whole new streets get notified. </p> 
     <pre>       That the access road beginning at the junction with Page Street,
       London, NW7 serving Copthall Leisure Centre and the
       surrounding properties shall be named:
       CHAMPIONS WAY, LONDON, NW4/NW7.
       That the access road that starts at Champions Way and ends at
       the Great North Way, London, NW4 serving Copthall Stadium
       shall be named:
       GREENLANDS LANE, LONDON, NW4.
</pre> 
     <p>These lists are not in a standard format among local authorities, and each local authority needs to be handled differently. I plan on writing a web scraping script to attempt to identify the changes, and by searching the nearby street names, pinpoint them on the map, so I would have a list of streets that need editing / surveying. <a href="/wiki/User:Welshie" title="User:Welshie">Welshie</a> 15:59, 13 November 2006 (UTC) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_Registry_Price_Paid_Data">Land Registry Price Paid Data</span></h4> 
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox" style="margin:2px 10%;background:#FDD;border:1px solid #AAA;border-left:10px #B22222 solid;">
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image" style="border:none;padding:2px 0;padding-left:0.9em;text-align:center">
         <div style="width:52px;">
          <img alt="Warning" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/40px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png" title="Warning" width="40" height="35" srcset="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/60px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png 1.5x, https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Ambox_warning_pn.svg/80px-Ambox_warning_pn.svg.png 2x">
         </div></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text" style="width:100%;border:none;padding:0.25em 0.9em;text-align:center;">This data <b>IS NOT OPEN DATA</b> in any useful meaning of the term: it is contaminated by PAF and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.gov.uk/government/statistical-data-sets/price-paid-data-downloads#when-using-or-publishing-our-price-paid-data">requires PAF licensing terms</a>. <b>DO NOT USE</b> the license is incompatible with OSM</td> 
       </tr>
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>Various facets of address-related data can be gleaned from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.gov.uk/dataset/land-registry-monthly-price-paid-data">Land Registry Price Paid Data</a>. Derek Jones provides <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://github.com/Derek-Jones/osm-house-numbers">example code</a> of an approach that can be taken to extract approximate house number positions. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_authority_data_sources">Local authority data sources</span></h4> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Fife">Fife</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fife.gov.uk/roads/index.cfm?fuseaction=aroads.list&amp;sr_town=75&amp;sr_road=+&amp;findRoad=GO">Roads database</a> Contains information like </p> 
     <div style="border:1px solid #aaa; margin-left:0.5em; padding:0.5em; overflow:auto">
      <pre>
Alburne Park (K8)  	 Glenrothes  	 Jct Woodside Way (C125) to Jct Prestonhall Drive (K8) / K9  	 Adopted  	K8
B969 (Part 01 Of 07) 	Glenrothes 	Southfield R/bout (B921) to 50 Mph Signs North Of Southfield R/bout 	Adopted 	B969
</pre>
     </div> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fife.gov.uk/atoz/index.cfm?fuseaction=atoz.list">As well as lots of other data</a>, including for example <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fife.gov.uk/atoz/index.cfm?fuseaction=factype.display&amp;objectid=BE612908-8785-11D6-9009-00508BDE7947">a list of public toilets</a> - for example <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fife.gov.uk/atoz/index.cfm?fuseaction=facility.display&amp;facid=B71330F0-FA1A-4203-936079BDCBE39E6E">a toilet in anstruther</a>. </p>
     <p>Also they offer a way to search for local facilities - <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.fife.gov.uk/yourtown/index.cfm">http://www.fife.gov.uk/yourtown/index.cfm</a> by postcode. This data could easily be extracted automatically, but the licences mentioned on the website are unsuitable (it's also unclear that this data is covered) and derivation from OS issues are also unclear. </p>
     <p>I have not contacted them. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="NaPTAN">NaPTAN</span></h4> 
     <p>The National Public Transport Access Nodes (NaPTAN) dataset contains details of some 350,000 public transport access points in Great Britain including bus stops, railway stations, tram stops and ferry terminals. See <a href="/wiki/NaPTAN" title="NaPTAN">NaPTAN</a> for more details. </p>
     <p><br> </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_England">Natural England</span></h4> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Natural_England" title="Natural England">Natural England</a> have <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gis.naturalengland.org.uk/pubs/gis/GIS_register.asp">datasets</a> containing boundaries of Open Access Land (Crow Act 2000), National Parks, SSSIs, National Nature Reserves, Marine Conservation Zones, and many other protected areas. It also has data on National Trails. On April 1st 2012 Natural England started releasing data under the Open Government Licence (OGL) therefore making it available for mapping in OpenStreetMap. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.naturalengland.org.uk/publications/data/gidatasetsfeature.aspx">Read more</a>, or view the <a href="/wiki/Natural_England" title="Natural England">wiki entry</a>. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FHRS">FHRS</span></h4> 
     <p>The Food Standards Agency produces machine readable versions of the Food Hygiene Rating System data. This ranks restaurants and businesses that sell or serve food or drink with a rating from 1 to 5. See <a href="/wiki/UK_Food_Hygiene_Rating_System" title="UK Food Hygiene Rating System">UK Food Hygiene Rating System</a> for details. </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Addresses_UK">Open Addresses UK</span></h4> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Open_Addresses_UK" title="Open Addresses UK">Open Addresses UK</a> is a UK government funded project by the Open Data institute to create an addresses dataset which is open licensed (free of the license complications of PAF and other royal mail/O.S. mess) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_Scotland">Transport Scotland</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.transportscotland.gov.uk/system/files/documents/tsc-basic-pages/High%20Load%20Grid%20-%2030%20March%202015.pdf">High Loads Grid</a> is a potential source of route relations - no explicit licence, so needs someone to contact. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguay">Uruguay</span></h3> 
     <p>The municipality of Montevideo approved a rule <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.imm.gub.uy/institucional/derecho-la-informacion">[36]</a> making all the data of that municipality (except the one that has privacy or security issues) public and free of copyright. In particular GIS data from the municipality of Montevideo is now available from its site<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://intgis.montevideo.gub.uy/sit/index.htm">[37]</a>. </p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S.">U.S.</span></h3> 
     <p>Check metadata for each shape file obtained from government sources, and search for "Use_Constraints:" or similar to help determine usability of data with OpenStreetMap. Many will list this as "None" and should be fine to use, but others from the same page will have varying constraints. When there is any doubt, ask the contact listed in the metadata for permision, and check with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wiki.openstreetmap.org/index.php/Mailing_lists">Legal Talk</a> mailing list. --<a href="/wiki/User:Dalep" title="User:Dalep">Dalep</a> 04:36, 2 September 2008 (UTC) </p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National">National</span></h4> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="TIGER">TIGER</span></h5> 
     <p><i>More detail on the <a href="/wiki/TIGER" title="TIGER">TIGER</a> page</i> </p>
     <p>The Tiger road data is imported </p>
     <p>The U.S. Census Bureau's TIGER geographic database covers the United States (including Puerto Rico). The data is available from the Census Bureau as TIGER/Line files in ASCII text format - <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.census.gov/geo/www/tiger/">http://www.census.gov/geo/www/tiger/</a>. ESRI shapefiles of the TIGER data is available at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.esri.com/data/download/census2000_tigerline/index.html">http://www.esri.com/data/download/census2000_tigerline/index.html</a> . </p>
     <p>The TIGER data are in the public domain - <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.census.gov/cgi-bin/geo/tigerfaq?Q11">http://www.census.gov/cgi-bin/geo/tigerfaq?Q11</a> . </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service"><a href="/wiki/US_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service_Data" title="US Fish and Wildlife Service Data">US Fish and Wildlife Service</a></span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.fws.gov/">USFWS</a> is a bureau of the federal government operated by the US Department of the Interior. USFWS makes cadastral data available at the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.fws.gov/gis/data/CadastralDB/index_cadastral.html">USFWS Geospatial Services</a> site. Refuges are accessible to the public for activities such as boating, hiking, hunting and fishing, so they are very relevant to OSM. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="US_Forest_Service"><a href="/wiki/US_Forest_Service_Data" title="US Forest Service Data">US Forest Service</a></span></h5> 
     <p>Many national forests have <a href="/wiki/US_Forest_Service_Data" title="US Forest Service Data">GIS data</a> available for download. A statement from region 6 (Pacific NW) <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.fs.fed.us/r6/data-library/gis/disclaimers.shtml">http://www.fs.fed.us/r6/data-library/gis/disclaimers.shtml</a> says that the data are public domain. Unfortunately each forest seems have their own index of data and data organization. There are some files very relevant to OSM (trails; recreation points listing campsites, docks etc) and some not so useful to the normal OSM reader (owl and fish habitats). </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="US_National_Park_Service"><a href="/wiki/US_National_Park_Service_Data" title="US National Park Service Data">US National Park Service</a></span></h5> 
     <p>The National Park Service has a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nps.gov/gis/data_info/">data clearinghouse</a> often with trails (some historic paths) rivers, roads and often with very high resolution orthophotos. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="USGS">USGS</span></h5> 
     <p>The USGS has a centralized database ( <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://seamless.usgs.gov">http://seamless.usgs.gov</a> ) that contains many data sets, several that would be of use to OSM, including very detailed surface water data sets (rivers, streams, lakes, tiny ponds), dams, federal lands . The data are in the public domain ( <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://seamless.usgs.gov/faq/general_faq.php#six">http://seamless.usgs.gov/faq/general_faq.php#six</a> ). However, they do request attribution of data to USGS, so it may require a followup to use in OSM. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Hydrography_Dataset">National Hydrography Dataset</span></h5> 
     <p>Part of the USGS Data, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hydrography_Dataset" title="National Hydrography Dataset">National Hydrography Dataset</a> contains detailed information on nearly all waterways and bodies in the United States </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="The_GAP_Analysis_Program">The GAP Analysis Program</span></h5> 
     <p>Also a project of the USGS, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gapanalysis.nbii.gov">The GAP Analysis Program</a> was conducted state by state initially and most recently on a regional basis. Relevant data includes landuse/landcover and stewardship/conservation lands, which includes military and DOD lands, and state/federal/local lands preserved for conservation purposes. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Department_of_Transportation_links">Department of Transportation links</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dot.state.ak.us/transpo_resources.shtml">DOT</a> homepage links for all 50 states. Check each for the GIS department, and statewide downloadable data. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="FAA_Digital_Obstacle_File_.28DOF.29">FAA Digital Obstacle File (DOF)</span></h5> 
     <p>The FAA Digital Obstacle File contains coordinates and elevations, as well as some meta data for aviation obstacles in the united states. It is distributed from the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.avn.faa.gov/index.asp?xml=naco/catalog/charts/digital/daicd">DAICD</a>. I believe that the data is public domain but the CD is sold as a subscription; someone like myself who has the CD could theoretically import the data into OSM without violating copyright. (TODO: double-check IP status.) <b>Update</b>: As of April 2015, the file is available online at <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://tod.faa.gov/tod/public/TOD_DOF.html">[38]</a>. </p>
     <p>The DOF would be a useful way to populate the map with aviation-chart-related items, particularly ones that can also serve as landmarks: smoke stacks, antennas, etc. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="FAA_National_Flight_Data_Center_.28NFDC.29">FAA National Flight Data Center (NFDC)</span></h5> 
     <p>Much aviation data is maintained at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nfdc.faa.gov/xwiki/bin/view/NFDC/Browse+Aeronautical+Data">nfdc.faa.gov</a>. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="CLUI_-_Centre_for_landuse_interpretation">CLUI - Centre for landuse interpretation</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.clui.org/clui_4_1/index.html">http://www.clui.org/clui_4_1/index.html</a> Information identifying weird landuses spotted in aerial imagery throughout the U.S. Non-profit organisation. No copyright information on their website. Didn't contact them (yet). Maps (approx landuse pinpointing) on the site uses google maps. May be use-able for vague identification purposes. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Agricultural_Imaging_Project">National Agricultural Imaging Project</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/FSA/apfoapp?area=home&amp;subject=prog&amp;topic=nai">http://www.fsa.usda.gov/FSA/apfoapp?area=home&amp;subject=prog&amp;topic=nai</a> </p>
     <p>Decent aerial imagery. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fsa.usda.gov/Internet/FSA_File/appendix_c.pdf">List of WMS servers</a> </p>
     <p><br> </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Mines">Mines</span></h5> 
     <p>Adding the list of mines and quarries in the USA from here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://tin.er.usgs.gov/mineplant/mineplant-fUS.kml">http://tin.er.usgs.gov/mineplant/mineplant-fUS.kml</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.data.gov/download/13/kml">http://www.data.gov/download/13/kml</a> </p>
     <p>Note, I have started the process to import this data, but I accidently overwrote the names with josm. Now I am working on modifying the names. <a class="external free" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/changeset/3345627">http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/changeset/3345627</a> </p>
     <p>keywords: EPA, Brownfields, Assessment Grant, Hazardous Substance, Property Redevelopment, public health, environment, federal data download, regulated sites, hazardous, contaminated, polluted, federal datasets, Land Revitalization, land redevelopment, land reuse, real property, hazardous substance, kmz, xml, Shapefile </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Next_Generation_Radar_.28NEXRAD.29_Locations">Next Generation Radar (NEXRAD) Locations</span></h5> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/nexradinv/">http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/nexradinv/</a> Next Generation Radar (NEXRAD) Locations <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.data.gov/details/4">http://www.data.gov/details/4</a> </p>
     <p>This geospatial rendering of weather radar sites gives access to an historical archive of Terminal Doppler Weather Radar data and is used primarily for research purposes. The archived data includes base data and derived products of the National Weather Service (NWS) Weather Surveillance Radar 88 Doppler (WSR-88D) next generation (NEXRAD) weather radar. Weather radar detects the three meteorological base data quantities: reflectivity, mean radial velocity, and spectrum width. From these quantities, computer processing generates numerous meteorological analysis products for forecasts, archiving and dissemination. There are 159 operational NEXRAD radar systems deployed throughout the United States and at selected overseas locations. At the Radar Operations Center (ROC) in Norman OK, personnel from the NWS, Air Force, Navy, and FAA use this distributed weather radar system to collect the data needed to warn of impending severe weather and possible flash floods; support air traffic safety and assist in the management of air traffic flow control; facilitate resource protection at military bases; and optimize the management of water, agriculture, forest, and snow removal. This data set is jointly owned by the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration, Federal Aviation Administration, and Department of Defense </p>
     <p><br> Processing&nbsp;: Unzip. Replace wsr with Placemark. gps babel. </p>
     <p>added these tags: </p>
     <p>source=<a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/nexradinv/">http://www.ncdc.noaa.gov/nexradinv/</a> radar_transponder=NEXRAD man_made = beacon </p>
     <p><a class="external free" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/changeset/3350339">http://www.openstreetmap.org/browse/changeset/3350339</a> </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="EPA_Geospatial_Data_Download:_Facility_and_Site_Information">EPA Geospatial Data Download: Facility and Site Information</span></h5> 
     <p>Contains information about facilities or sites subject to environmental regulation, including key facility information along with associated environmental interests for use in mapping and reporting applications. </p>
     <p>keywords&nbsp;: FRS, EPA, CERCLIS, NEPT, NPDES, PCS, RCRA, RCRAInfo, Superfund, NPL, TRI, regulated sites, toxic release, major discharges, brownfields, federal data download, national priorities list, public health, environment, federal datasets, kmz, xml, shapefile, sites, facilities </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.data.gov/download/6/kml">http://www.data.gov/download/6/kml</a> </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.epa.gov/enviro/geo_data.html">http://www.epa.gov/enviro/geo_data.html</a> </p>
     <p>See here for the full record&nbsp;: <a href="/wiki/EPAGeospatial" title="EPAGeospatial">EPAGeospatial</a> </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Atlas_Raw_Data_Download_Site">National Atlas Raw Data Download Site</span></h5> 
     <p>This site contains a huge amount of data possibly useful to OSM. Place names, political boundaries, hydrology, etc. Most data is USGS collected and is public domain, however the site "Web Policies" page states that copyright must be inspected for each data set. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.nationalatlas.gov/atlasftp.html">http://www.nationalatlas.gov/atlasftp.html</a> </p>
     <p><b>Note</b>: Many of the shapefiles on nationalatlas.gov, particularly fedlanp020.shp and its derivatives, are horribly inaccurate (the resolution is low). Please <b>avoid importing any more of it onto OSM!</b> Users have found boundaries as much as a mile off from their true location. See <a class="external text" href="http://www.openstreetmap.org/user/SamatJain/diary/11578">this diary post</a>. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Wilderness.net">Wilderness.net</span></h5> 
     <p>Wilderness.net gathers US Designated Wilderness area definitions from the US Forest Service, Fish and Game, National Park Service and Bureau of Land Management into a single data set available for free download as Shapefile or KML. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.wilderness.net/index.cfm?fuse=NWPS&amp;sec=advSearch">http://www.wilderness.net/index.cfm?fuse=NWPS&amp;sec=advSearch</a> </p>
     <p>Wilderness.net webmaster Lisa Eidson has been contacted and confirmed that all Wilderness data available on Wilderness.net is public domain. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Transportation_Atlas_Database">National Transportation Atlas Database</span></h5> 
     <p>The NTAD maintains various datasets associated with transportation in the US. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.rita.dot.gov/bts/sites/rita.dot.gov.bts/files/publications/national_transportation_atlas_database/index.html">http://www.rita.dot.gov/bts/sites/rita.dot.gov.bts/files/publications/national_transportation_atlas_database/index.html</a> </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="HPMS.2FARNOLD">HPMS/ARNOLD</span></h5> 
     <p>The <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FHWA" class="extiw" title="w:FHWA">FHWA</a> provides the ARNOLD (All Roads Network Of Linear referenced Data) data under the HPMS (Highway Performance Monitoring System); see <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openstreetmap.us/2014/12/arnold-for-osm/">here</a>. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.fhwa.dot.gov/policyinformation/hpms/shapefiles.cfm">http://www.fhwa.dot.gov/policyinformation/hpms/shapefiles.cfm</a> </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="NOAA_ENC_wreck_and_AWOIS_database">NOAA ENC wreck and AWOIS database</span></h5> 
     <p>The NOAA Office of Coast Survey maintains a database of wrecks and underwater obstructions. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.nauticalcharts.noaa.gov/hsd/wrecks_and_obstructions.html">[39]</a> The data itself is useful for a nautical chart like in the OpenSeaMap project. After confirming with NOAA via email, the data is indeed in the public domain and therefore can be imported into OSM. </p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="California">California</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://frap.cdf.ca.gov/data/frapgisdata/select.asp?theme=3">CalFire</a> has a set of landcover layers that can be imported. The website says they may be distributed in any manner but a credit must be given. See <a href="/wiki/California_Land_Cover" title="California Land Cover">California_Land_Cover</a>. </p>
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://gis.ca.gov/BrowseCatalog.epl">http://gis.ca.gov/BrowseCatalog.epl</a> has state park info and more </p>
     <p>California has a master list of all parks on all levels - federal, state, county and city <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.calands.org">http://www.calands.org</a>. We still need to get permission from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.greeninfo.org/">GreenInfo</a> to import data. </p>
     <p>To see the counties that have granted OSM permission to use their data, go to <a href="/wiki/California/Import" title="California/Import">California/Import</a>. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="County_of_Los_Angeles">County of Los Angeles</span></h5> 
     <p>Los Angeles County provides <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://egis3.lacounty.gov/dataportal/2011/04/28/countywide-building-outlines/">countywide building outlines</a> in public domain; data was collected from 2006-2008. More recent data exists, but has not been publicly released. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="City_of_San_Jose">City of San Jose</span></h5> 
     <p>San Jose provides a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sanjoseca.gov/index.aspx?NID=3308">wide variety of datasets</a> which includes building footprints, parcels, address points, streets, sanitary and storm systems among others. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="City_of_Berkeley">City of Berkeley</span></h5> 
     <p>Berkeley provides a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://data.cityofberkeley.info/City-Government/Roofprints-2006/gnp8-t9x8">citywide dataset of building roof prints</a>. This data was collected in 2006. </p> 
     <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="City_of_Fremont">City of Fremont</span></h5> 
     <p>Fremont has <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://egis-cofgis.opendata.arcgis.com/datasets/5b4a263844634084af2001f82a5174a5_0">open dataset of building footprints</a> that covers the entire city area. </p>

     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dcgis.dc.gov/dcgis/site/default.asp?dcgisNav=%7C30632%7C">DC GIS</a> Main page. The GIS Data Clearinghouse/Catalog link contains hundreds of data layers. </p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span></h4> 
     <p>Florida Department of Transportation GIS data in shape format. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dot.state.fl.us/planning/statistics/gis/">Web site</a>, and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="ftp://ftp.dot.state.fl.us/fdot/co/planning/transtat/gis/shapefiles/">direct FTP</a> Everything provided by the FDOT GIS is in public domain, this has been verified by e-mail. </p>
     <p>Aerial photography is also available upon request from FDOT's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dot.state.fl.us/surveyingandmapping/apac.shtm">Surveying &amp; Mapping Office</a>. The images, provided in <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MrSID" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:MrSID">MrSID</a> format, are much higher quality than Yahoo's aerials and are released in the public domain, verified by email. The entire state is covered, with most counties photographed as recently as 2008, but check their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dot.state.fl.us/surveyingandmapping/aerialmap/AerialStatus.pdf">coverage map</a> to find out for specific counties. Unfortunately, the common OSM editing tools don't support MrSID, but with some effort, the files can be converted and served through a standard WMS. </p>
     <p>A site for tracking down other sources of data in Florida is <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.findgis.com/">FindGIS</a>, a blog/site that is pursuing Florida government agencies to release their GIS data as required. As well as list where that data can be found. Not all is free, or released as Public Domain. See each site individually. </p>
     <p>NOTE about <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.cfgis.org/">http://www.cfgis.org/</a> Careful reading suggests they are claiming copyright (and limiting distribution) on behalf of the data sources they have in the Clearinghouse even for sources that are/should be public domain. Further inquires should be made before using anything downloaded from here, or check the original source. </p>
     <p>Counties listed below for more detailed information layers, better accuracy and up to date roads. Just be careful of the datum for the county data. </p>

     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hawaii">Hawaii</span></h4> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hawaii.gov/dbedt/gis/">Hawaii Statewide GIS Program</a> </p>
     <p>The Hawaii GIS Program has a very large collection of GIS data. No license information is mentioned on the website, but the GIS data is all in the public domain, as verified in a personal conversation with a manager in the GIS department. </p>
     <p>The road data is probably not particularly relevant, since TIGER road data has already been imported. But this source includes data that would be very difficult or impossible to get any other way, such as streams and coral reefs. </p>
